Shanghai Municipal Council Revises Regulations for Chartered Rickshaw Licenses

明年元旦起實行

Effective from New Year's Day Next Year

The Shanghai Municipal Council has recently revised the licensing regulations for private rickshaws (i.e., chartered rickshaws) in accordance with the newly established principles to ensure consistency. The revised regulations will be implemented starting on January 1st. The provisions regarding the license plates on the vehicles will be implemented starting on April 1st. According to the regulations, chartered rickshaw licenses can only be issued for vehicles used by the owner for personal use or those hired for at least one month. Applicants applying for or renewing licenses must declare in writing that the vehicle is for personal use only; however, family members may also use it. If the applicant is a company or firm, the vehicle may not be used for the transportation of persons outside of the organization.

Those pulling chartered rickshaws must be licensed rickshaw pullers. The employer's name and vehicle number must be indicated on the rickshaw puller's license. If a vehicle is to employ more than one rickshaw puller, prior written permission from the Shanghai Municipal Council is required. Licensees must not allow their vehicles to be rented out or used to solicit passengers. Vehicles must not be used for advertising purposes, and must not be equipped with horns or other sound-producing devices. Licensees must report any changes of address to the Shanghai Municipal Council. Rickshaw pullers must be given a copy of the "Notice to Chartered Rickshaw Pullers" and instructed on the regulations to be followed.

Starting from April 1st of next year, chartered rickshaws will be issued with enamel license plates with white characters on a black background, which will be affixed to the left side of the vehicle. If the license plate is damaged or lost, a replacement will be issued upon payment of one silver dollar. In addition to the license plate, a small colored tag will be issued each quarter and affixed to the vehicle along with the license plate. The license plates are the property of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and the licensee is responsible for their safekeeping. They must be returned to the issuing office when not in use. The license fee must be paid as long as the license plate is registered in the licensee's name, regardless of whether the vehicle is in use or not.

Chartered rickshaw licenses issued by the Shanghai Municipal Council are valid in the French Concession. However, residents should apply for licenses from the Public Concession or the French Concession depending on their place of residence. For companies or firms applying for licenses, the location of their principal office will determine where they should apply.

Reduced Freight Charges for Factory Machinery and Tools

一月一日起施行

Effective from January 1st

The Directorate General of Railways received a telegram from the Ministry of Railways stating that in order to encourage domestic factories along the railway lines, machinery and tools should be subject to reduced freight charges. The various railways previously submitted their opinions and proposed reduction methods to the Ministry, which were approved by the First Railway Joint Transportation Price Research Conference: (1) Machinery used by domestic-capital factories along the railway lines, whether newly built or expanded, will be charged one grade lower than the listed machinery in the classification table, except for those otherwise specified. (2) Agricultural tools will continue to be charged at 80% of the regular rate. The above should be approved and implemented from January 1st of the 24th year. In addition to distribution, the bureau has ordered the Transportation Department to comply.

Shanghai Iron Works Creates "Kai" Character Electric Sock Knitting Machine

The Shanghai Iron Works, located at Gaoyang Temple, West Zhalankou, in this city, concerned about the backwardness of knitting machinery in our country, relying on more than ten years of manufacturing experience and two years of dedicated research, has successfully developed a new type of "Kai" character electric automatic sock knitting machine, adding a brilliant touch to China's knitting industry. The machine has five major advantages: (1) The sock knitting machine is fully automatic from the opening to the tip, without manual labor; (2) One person can manage five to ten machines, which is simple and labor-saving; (3) It produces men's and women's long socks quickly and at a low cost; (4) The socks are neat and have a suitable tightness, surpassing hand-operated machines many times over; (5) The labor cost for knitting various silk and wool socks is only four cents per dozen. Since the factory created the "Kai" character electric sock machine, knitting factories in various ports have purchased and used them, praising them unanimously as a powerful tool to resist foreign goods. The factory's distribution office is located at No. 202 Caishi Road, French Concession.

The new Consul will allow the opening of gambling dens in the Concession in view of the declining market in the Concession, with the aim of defrauding bribes. Eight members of the fraudulent gang have been arrested and sent to court for interrogation and investigation. The details of the case have been briefly reported. It is now known that the mastermind behind this case is Yang Yingchu (58 years old), a Cantonese residing at No. 13, Dakangfang, Baier Road, French Concession. Recently, he has been impoverished and bored. Upon learning that the current French Consul General will be taking leave to return to his country, he took the opportunity to spread rumors that the new Consul, in order to

Revitalize the Concession's Economy,

has been approved by the French government to allow the opening of five gambling dens in the French Concession. At the same time, he colluded with his fellow villager, Pan Shucan (32 years old, residing at No. 61, Sichuanli, Sichuan Road), to impersonate an advisor to Mr. Gu Weijun, the Chinese Minister to France, falsely claiming that Pan could arrange for the movement to obtain a letter of introduction. At the same time, Yang ordered Cai Binshan (34 years old, from Pudong, residing at No. 226 Caishi Road, French Concession, who was previously arrested and sent to court for a flower society case with a Mr. Hua, but was acquitted due to lack of evidence) to find capitalists to invest in opening gambling tables. Cai then entrusted Yang Dingguo (40 years old, from Guangdong, residing at No. 61, Hongli, Roberts Road) to find investors. Yang then, based on Cai's words,

Engaged in Extensive Planning and Promotion.

The matter was discovered by the French Police, who dispatched interpreter Jiang Futian, disguised as the accountant of capitalist Hong Bingan, and Zhang Zhongan, representing his employer Hong Bingan, to Room 202 of the Dadong Hotel on West Xinqiao Street on the afternoon of December 30th to invite Yang Dingguo to negotiate. Yang then invited Yang Yingchu and Pan Shucan to the scene. Pan claimed to be an advisor to Minister Gu, and Yang Yingchu and Pan told Jiang Futian, the disguised representative of the fake capitalist, that they could issue letters of introduction. Two letters had already been taken by someone surnamed Sun, and there were three more, each requiring a capital of one million yuan to be deposited in the bank. After the Consul General and Deputy Consul General confirmed the reality, the letters of introduction could be signed and issued, subject to a monthly payment of 225,000 yuan. At the same time, an "activity fee" of 45,000 yuan must be paid for each letter of introduction, and it was said that 35,000 yuan of this sum had to be handed over, with 10,000 yuan going to

Those Handling the Matter.

"You need to raise the money quickly, it shouldn't be delayed." At that time, Jiang feigned agreement and replied that he could discuss it with his employer, and agreed to talk again the next day. That night, they went to the Guangdong restaurant Tiantian Restaurant on Sichuan Road for dinner and dispersed. The next day, December 1, at noon, Jiang again invited Yang Dingguo to Room 301 of the Dafang Hotel at No. 33 Zhengjia Muqiao Street to discuss the matter. Yang then telephoned the Wu Palace Hotel and invited Yang Yingchu, Cai Binshan, Pan Shucan, and their accomplices Wang Boqing (50 years old, from Guangdong, residing at No. 1319 Roberts Road), Fu Fengshan (33 years old, from Guangdong, residing at No. 18 Yong'an Street), Pi Xichun (44 years old, from Hunan, residing at Room 25 of the Yixin Commercial Inn on Hunan Road), and Zhu Zhenhua (36 years old, from Changzhou, residing at No. 4 Hongfa Lane, Roberts Road) to the scene. At the same time, the police ordered interpreter Li Xianyang

To Disguise Himself as a Capitalist,

Hong Bingan, to the scene. On the other hand, they dispatched gambling detectives Cai Zongyi, He Zongyu, Zhu Junpei, Liu Delin, and Tan Rongxuan, led by detective leader Hang Bingquan, to lie in ambush in the Dafang Hotel. The two interpreters, Jiang and Li, who had been sent by the police to disguise themselves as capitalists, waited for Yang Yingchu and others to arrive before proceeding to negotiate all the conditions, agreeing to all of them. Yang and others then ordered that the capital of one million yuan be deposited in the Shanghai Bank and instructed that a long-term account be opened in the name of the group for them to carry out the procedures for obtaining the license. By evening, after the two parties had negotiated the conditions in detail, they signed a contract, agreeing that one party would raise funds and organize a gambling den, and the other party would carry out the procedures for obtaining the license. By the time the contract was signed, it was already 8:30 PM, and both parties

Were About to Disperse.

The undercover detectives who had been sent by the French Police came out and arrested Yang Yingchu, Cai Baoshan, Yang Dingguo, Pan Shucan, and their accomplices, a total of eight people, on the spot, without missing a single one. A document regarding the organization of a flower society was found on Yang Yingchu's person, and a contract document for organizing flower society gambling was also found during a search of Cai Baoshan's home. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. The case has been thoroughly investigated by the police, and the statements of each person have been recorded. Yesterday, Sun Penghang, a judge from the Eighth Criminal Division of the Second Special Court, presided over the hearing. Yuan Jiahong, the police lawyer, stated the facts of the case and said that the first and fourth defendants, Yang Yingchu and Cai Baoshan,

Habitually Committed Fraud.

The police charged them with fraud under Article 364 of the Criminal Code, and the remaining defendants were charged with fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Code. At this point, official witness Jiang Futian appeared in court, and after being sworn in, he testified to the circumstances of being ordered to disguise himself as a representative of the capitalist and negotiating with the defendants Yang Dingguo, Yang Yingchu, Cai Baoshan, Pan Shucan, and others. Later, the court instructed the police to charge the first and fourth defendants under Article 364 of the Criminal Code, but there were problems with the handling of the case, so the court ruled that the case would be adjourned and transferred to the local court for trial at 9:00 AM on the 7th. The defendants were returned to custody.

江海關昨布各週知

The Jianghai Customs Issued a Public Notice Yesterday

Tang Haian, the Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Bertheau, the Customs Commissioner, issued a joint notice No. 1409 yesterday regarding the exemption of import taxes on old Chinese and foreign stamps: "Now, in compliance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, all old Chinese and foreign stamps imported from December 3rd of this year will be exempt from import tax. This is hereby notified to all merchants and people."

The Xin Renhe Tragedy: Private Lawsuit Partially Settled

以一千四百元了結

Settled for 1,400 Yuan

當庭繕就筆錄簽字

Minutes Prepared and Signed in Court

In March of last year, the Xin Renhe steamship of the Yu Yu Shipping Company in Nanshi, while sailing from Haimen back to Shanghai, tied up five peddlers on board, including Mei Laoer and Ma Koubao, with lead wire, attached them to large rocks, placed them in sacks, and threw them into the sea to drown. After the tragedy occurred, the victims' families learned of the previous situation and were extremely saddened and angry. They filed a lawsuit in the local court, and the ship's owner, Sun Xingsheng, the comprador, Chen Baosheng, and the bookkeeper and sailors were arrested, interrogated, and sentenced to life imprisonment or varying terms of imprisonment. In the private lawsuit portion, a judgment of over ten thousand yuan was issued, with each defendant jointly liable. Sun and others refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, which ordered the case to be sent to Suzhou for trial. Recently, the court arrested two other crew members, Wu A'er and Li San, who were accomplices, interrogated them, and sentenced them to await instructions. It is now known that the private lawsuit portion has not yet been resolved. Recently, new employees on the ship and others, feeling that the families of the victims were all suffering, and that Sun Xingsheng and others had been imprisoned for a long time, and that their families were in dire straits, no less than the families of the victims, repeatedly negotiated and raised funds to distribute to the families of the victims to help them live. However, none of them were willing to come forward. Fan Si Rongqing came forward and was willing to act as a representative, entrusting lawyer Guo Yihua to submit a statement to the court, stating that funds had been raised for condolence. After receiving the submission, the court specially opened the Second Court yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, presided over by Judge Wang Run. The plaintiffs who reported to the court included Mei You (27 years old, from Hubei, wife of the deceased Mei Laoer), Zhou Ma (i.e., Zhang Ma, 32 years old, from Pinghu, wife of the deceased Zhou Jinsheng), Shen Zhou (48 years old, from Zhenjiang, wife of the deceased Shen Xianzhang), Ma Liu (43 years old, from Rugao, mother of the deceased Ma Koubao), and Wei Zhu (52 years old, from Anhui, mother of the deceased Wei Jinren). After the judge took his seat, he ordered each of the victims' families to come to the case and briefly interrogated them, according to which each of the corpses claimed that because the ship was carrying contraband items, it was seized by the police and thought to be reported by the deceased and others, so five people were brutally killed. Our livelihood has been cut off. When they finished speaking, they all wept sadly. Then, lawyer Guo stated that colleagues of the Yu Xing Company were now willing to offer condolences of 1,400 yuan, which had been agreed upon with the opposing lawyer Yu, and had been agreed to by the victims' families. The judge asked each of the victims' families, and there were no objections. They claimed that they requested to withdraw the private lawsuit and that they urgently wanted to return to their hometown to live. After the interrogating official obtained the confession, he prepared the minutes and ordered each of the victims' families to affix their fingerprints in court. At the same time, lawyer Guo presented a check for 1,400 yuan to the court. After the interrogating official examined it, he transferred it to lawyer Yu for collection. The victims' families thanked him and left.

The Railway Bureau Absolutely Prohibits Waiters on Railway Dining Cars from Accepting Tips

餐費收條上蓋有戳記

The Receipt for Meals Is Stamped

In addition to the cost of meals, passengers on the railway often give tips to the waiters. The Transportation Department believes that the dining car employees are hired and paid by the railway, and all services such as serving meals are their inherent responsibilities. The bad habit of demanding tips should be completely eradicated. Even if passengers voluntarily give tips, they should not be accepted without authorization in order to set an example of integrity. Therefore, the managers of each dining car have been notified that if any waiter is found to be soliciting tips from passengers in the future, in addition to severely punishing the offending waiter, the manager on duty will also be held jointly responsible. Even if passengers are willing to give tips, they should be politely declined and not accepted. On the other hand, the meal receipts are stamped with the words "Tipping is strictly prohibited, please help us maintain this," in order to prevent passengers from repeating old habits. Railway colleagues can also act as supervisors when riding the train to help with the rectification.

Wu Nailong, a Teacher at Nanyang Advanced Commercial School, Dies After Jumping from a Window

患病甚重𤍠度驟增

Seriously Ill with a Sudden Increase in Temperature

神經頓變態所致

Caused by a Sudden Change in Mental State

Wu Nailong, a 21-year-old Cantonese teacher at the Nanyang Advanced Commercial School on Shanhai Pass Road, lived at No. 1, Zhenqing Lane, Chuan Highway, Zhabei. Two weeks ago, Wu suffered from typhoid fever and was quite ill. Although he had consulted doctors, he had not yet recovered. Because there were many people in his family, the patient inevitably felt disturbed, so on the 11th of this month, his mother, Wu Lu, and others accompanied Nailong to the Shanghai Sanatorium Hospital on Bafu Road and resided in Room 400 on the fourth floor for treatment. Unexpectedly, the illness worsened suddenly the night before last, and the temperature suddenly increased to 105 degrees, causing his nerves to suddenly become abnormal. He walked to the window, jumped out, and fell to the ground. He died immediately due to severe injuries. After Chen Xuezhi, a nurse at the hospital, noticed it, she immediately reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, which ordered Chinese Detective Feng Qi to investigate. He then carried the body to the Feilun Road Verification Office. Yesterday morning, Tang, the prosecutor, was appointed by the First Special District Local Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wu Zuyi, to visit the office and verify the body. According to Chinese Captain Zhu Mengwei's report of the previous situation, Tang ordered that the deceased Nailong, male, had suffered from an illness and died from a fall. The body was handed over to Wu Yuanlong, Wu's brother, for coffin burial after he signed a statement.

已通過籌備委員會大綱

The Outline of the Preparatory Committee Has Been Approved

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the Shanghai Chinese Benevolent Association had suggested to the two internal education departments the organizational outline of the China Children's Year Preparatory Committee, and the clothing and jewelry of the preparatory committee members, which were quite fashionable. Ning, a teacher who recently returned home, arrived in Shanghai yesterday and brought many local products from Ningbo. At about 9:00 AM yesterday morning, he planned to give a part of the local products to his family member, Zhang Yaozhang, who lives at No. 1, Taikang Lane, Dalin Road, Xiaoximen, who currently works at Qianxin Foreign Firm. Unexpectedly, just as he was about to carry the items out of the door, a bandit wearing a blue cloth short coat suddenly jumped out from the side of the road and followed him to the back door of No. 1 Taikang Lane. He took out a pistol and forbade him to make a sound, and snatched a gold bracelet worth more than 50 yuan from Yuan's arm. He then shouted for help. The lane guard, Ma Haiji, heard the alarm and chased after him, grabbing the bandit. The bandit, in desperation, fired a shot to warn him. Forged Bill of Lading - Illicit Removal of a Large Quantity of Tea

Colluding with Brokers for Sales

A Portion of the Stolen Goods Recovered

Zhang Wanquan, a Cantonese residing at No. 12, Lane 96, Jing'an Temple Road, is the owner of the Lily Wah Tea Company. All tea belonging to the company is stored at the Tiancheng Tea Warehouse, No. 7, Lane 576, North Shanxi Road. Normally, to withdraw tea, Zhang would stamp and write a bill of lading and present it for collection. Yu Yingxing, formerly an old clerk at Zhang's company, but now dismissed, still occasionally visited Zhang's residence for leisure. On the 8th of this month, Zhang wanted to withdraw a box of tea from the Tiancheng Tea Warehouse as a sample to sell to various colleagues. Because Zhang was not good at writing, he instructed Yu to write a bill of lading, which Zhang stamped, ordering him to collect the tea from Tiancheng. Unexpectedly, Yu had ill intentions and secretly hid the box of tea he withdrew. On one hand, he falsely told Zhang that the bill of lading was lost. On the other hand, he secretly forged the Lily Wah Tea Company's seal, wrote a bill of lading, and on the 9th, withdrew 26 boxes of tea from the Tiancheng Tea Warehouse, totaling a value of $694.50. He colluded with a broker from Huizhou, Wang Xiuchuan, and sold the tea to Zhu Yizhi, owner of the Yongxiang Tea Company, No. 77, Yuqing Lane, Tianshui Road, obtaining $416.70, which he spent. Zhang Wanquan learned of this and reported it to the Mixed Court Police Station, which dispatched detectives Yang Zhaoqing and Ma Ya to arrest Wang Xiuchuan in Zhabei the day before yesterday and bring him back to the police station. However, Yu Yingxing is still at large. Subsequently, guided by Wang, 26 boxes of the original stolen tea were recovered from the Zhengtai Tea Warehouse, No. 12, Pengcheng Lane, North Henan Road, and a box of tea and an empty box were found at the No. 5 Tea Market, Lane 313, Qipu Road, and all were transported back to the police station for temporary storage. Yesterday morning, Wang Xiuchuan was sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court to be prosecuted for forgery under Article 233 of the Criminal Law. First, the police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, presented the case and requested a postponement. Zhang Wanquan also complained about Yu and others forging the seal and illicitly withdrawing goods. Zhu Yizhi, owner of the Yongxiang Company, testified that the tea was brought to him by broker Wang Xiuchuan, who claimed to be the manager of the Lily Wah Tea Company, and asked him to sell it. He bought it at the market price, at $20 per dan, for a total of $416.70. When questioned, Wang Xiuchuan confessed that the tea was brought by Yu Yingxing, who claimed to be the manager of the Lily Wah Tea Company, and asked him to sell it. He only received a commission of $30, and Yu took the rest of the money. After verification of the confession by Judge Liu Yugui, Wang was allowed to be released on bail of $400 and to appear whenever summoned. The case was postponed for seven days for further hearing.

Kidnapping of the Dingsheng Comprador Case Solved - Li Shanting's Coffin Arrives in Shanghai

The Case Was Solved After Two Years and Four Months

The Ring Leader Injured His Paramour's Husband, The Wife and Her Husband Reported Him Out of Extreme Anger

The Dingsheng ship, belonging to Jardine Matheson & Co., was stolen in Tianjin, taking the comprador Li Shanting and the dockside accountant Zhang, on August 13th of the year before last. Two years and four months passed without solving the case. Now, the main culprit has been arrested in Tianjin. Li Shanting was killed and his body arrived in Shanghai yesterday. The matter is quite tortuous. The details are as follows:

Revisit the Old Matter

The Dingsheng ship of British merchant Jardine Matheson & Co. was a regular Northern shipping vessel. The ship arrived at Tanggu, Tianjin on August 13th (year 21 of the Republic). Li Shanting was in the ship's accounting office. At around 5 p.m., several cars suddenly arrived, and the ring leader led his gang onto the ship to kidnap Li. Li locked the accounting office door, and the bandits could not open it, so they shot off the cabin door lock, then entered and took Li onto the car and fled. Zhang, the dockside accountant, was also kidnapped.

Zhang Shot Dead First

After the case occurred, the British consulate negotiated with the North China authorities, ordering them to rescue Zhang and Li, and to eliminate the bandits. The Tianjin military and police authorities obtained a tip and discovered the bandit's lair more than 40 miles from Tianjin. A team was dispatched to suppress them, and a confrontation occurred. Zhang, the dockside accountant, was nearly 60 years old and escaped from the bandit's nest, but was shot dead by the bandits on the way. Li Shanting was kidnapped by the ring leader and escaped. This occurred during the winter of that year. Since then, there has been no news of Li's whereabouts.

Bandit's Wife Turns Against Him

The ring leader was rumored to be a military officer from a defeated warlord. He took Li Shanting and fled, and his wife and others were in Tianjin. Later, due to the lack of news, the bandit's wife suspected that her husband was dead and had an affair with another man in Tianjin. Until October of this year, when the case was fading, the ring leader secretly returned to Tianjin to look for his wife. He heard that she had already had an affair with someone and had a major conflict with the paramour. The ring leader used a pistol to injure the paramour. His wife turned against him and reported to the military authorities, stating the facts of the kidnapping for ransom and resisting officers two years ago. An old case from over two years ago was solved due to a dispute over a wife.

Li's Body Discovered

The ring leader was arrested by the Tianjin authorities in October. The reason for kidnapping Li Shanting, the comprador of Dingsheng, was investigated. The bandit said that Li refused to send a letter to his family to pay a huge sum, so he was shot dead. The bandit collected the body and buried it in a coffin worth over $130, intending to use it as a step to make his family pay a ransom to redeem the body. Later, the coffin was located and examined, and after confirmation, the military and police authorities notified the Tianjin branch of Jardine Matheson & Co., and wired Shanghai, ordering Li's family to go to Tianjin to claim the body and return to Shanghai for burial.

Coffin Transported to Shanghai

After Li Shanting's wife received the news, she went to Tianjin to claim her husband's body and escorted the coffin to Shanghai for burial. Li's wife went north on the Dingsheng ship, and now she has received her husband's coffin and is returning to Shanghai on the Dingsheng ship. It was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on Wednesday, but was delayed by one day due to fog on the way. It entered the port at 6:30 a.m. yesterday and arrived at the dock at about 8 a.m., where it was unloaded and prepared to be transported to the ancestral home for burial.

Cheng Yushu Accuses Sang Zhichuan of Abandonment

Fifty Years Old and Still Seeking Pleasure

Abandonment Soon After Giving Birth

Sang Zhichuan, a Ningbo native residing at No. 58, Changyun Lane, No. 468, Dagu Road, is 56 years old and runs a leather trunk shop. He has many children who have grown up and started families. However, Sang, past his prime, still indulged in seeking pleasure outside. On September 1st of last year, he met Cheng Yushu, a Cantonese woman, who was only twenty years old. Sang immediately seduced her to a hotel and committed adultery. Because Sang had a wife, Cheng could only become a concubine. She rented a house outside and lived secretly. In a few months, Cheng became pregnant. On July 4th of this year, she gave birth to a son at the Zhongde Hospital. Unexpectedly, Sang recently changed his behavior and not only ignored Cheng's life but also beat and abused her. Cheng Yushu hired a lawyer and filed a criminal complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing Sang Zhichuan and his eldest son, Sang Jianzhang, second son, Sang Jianheng, third son, Fuyuan, and Fuyuan's wife, Ms. Hu, of abandonment and encroachment, and also filed a civil lawsuit for $18,700. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi presided over the trial at the Eighth Criminal Division. Of the five defendants, only Sang Zhichuan appeared in court. The plaintiff, Sang Cheng Yushu, held her five-month-old child and claimed that on September 1st of last year, Sang Zhichuan forcibly raped her at the Central Hotel and stated that he already had a wife, advising her to temporarily become a concubine. She had no choice but to agree. On October 1st, she rented a room at No. 361, Dahua Apartment, and began living together. About two months later, on December 22nd, she moved to his home at No. 86, Changyun Lane, Dagu Road. As soon as she arrived at his home, she was resented by his sons and daughters-in-law. First, they insulted her, then they used force and beat her. At that time, they went to the Xinza Gate Police Station, and the head instructed them to return for self-mediation. That evening, his sons and daughters-in-law robbed all her belongings and drove her away. Later, after mediation, she made peace with Sang Zhichuan and continued to live together at No. 39, Ronggui Lane, Avenue Haig. Before half a month had passed, another rift occurred. Because she had nowhere to live, she temporarily resided at No. 22, Xinshun Lane, Changan Road, Zhabei, at the home of her foster father, Wang Jinshan. All her daily expenses were also paid by Wang. Unexpectedly, on the 21st of last month, Sang gathered a crowd and suddenly came to her place, making all kinds of noise and forcing her to go with him, causing a major dispute on the way. The police took them to the Fourth District Police Bureau, where Sang pointed her out as his runaway concubine, who had taken his belongings worth over $600, resulting in her being detained. Later, she was transferred to the court prosecutor's office for investigation, which resulted in a decision not to prosecute. Therefore, she is now filing a lawsuit, accusing Sang and others of abandonment and encroachment, and requesting that they be punished according to the law. When questioned, Sang Zhichuan confessed that the plaintiff was his concubine, but now his legal wife had committed suicide because of the plaintiff, so she could be made his legal wife. The child she was holding was indeed his. Now, he could order her to go home, otherwise she was committing adultery with Wang Jin, occupying another man's wife, and taking someone's child, and should be investigated. Judge Wu advised the plaintiff to go home, but she resolutely refused, only requesting that the law be strictly enforced. The court ordered that the case be postponed for seven days, pending the summons of Sang Jianzhang and others for further hearing.

Shanghai Bank - Handling Tobacco Loans in Shandong Province

Organizing Production and Sales Cooperatives to Be Established Within the Year

Cotton Loans in Shaanxi Province Will Expand in Amount

In recent years, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank has been quite active in investing in rural areas. Recently, it plans to provide tobacco loans in Qingzhou and Xuzhou, Shandong Province. The existing cotton cooperative in Shaanxi will expand its organization and increase the amount of investment. The details are as follows:

Handling Tobacco Loans in Shandong Province

According to the bank's spokesperson, the output of silk tobacco in Shandong Province is increasing daily. There are more than 300 production and sales cooperatives in Linzi and other places. The results of the silkworm loans issued by the bank through the cooperatives last year were very satisfactory. Recently, it is planned to establish a tobacco production and sales cooperative in Qingzhou, with the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute responsible for production guidance, the Shandong Provincial Construction Department responsible for organization, and the bank responsible for loans. It can be established within the year, preparing for the tobacco loans.

Expanding Investment in Shaanxi Province

In addition, the six major cotton production and sales cooperatives established by the bank in Shaanxi Province and the eight major cooperatives organized by the China Continent and other five banks have had very poor results since the cotton loans began. The borrowers and lenders have a good relationship. In order to expand the scope of its loans, the bank plans to add several cooperatives next year. After the Closure of Chengchang Native Cloth Store

Large Deposit Amounts, Creditors Continue to File Lawsuits

Chengchang Native Cloth Store, a well-known store in the South City of Shanghai, was affected by the January 28th Incident, and its business was sluggish. Subsequently, in February of the 22nd year, it entrusted accountant Chao Jimei and lawyer Xue Lisheng to announce liquidation. However, Chengchang was an old store with decades of business and had annual profits. Because its credit was solid, it had many deposits in various places. Once it suddenly announced liquidation and repaid debts proportionally, the creditors protested. At that time, six creditors, including Chen Xiuji, had deposits of more than 10,000 and hired a lawyer separately to file a lawsuit against the store's manager, Qiao Qiupu. However, because Qiao Qiupu had no assets to execute, there were no results. Now, Chen Xiuji and others have learned that Chengchang is a partnership store, and its shareholders, such as Zhou Chunji and Li Xinji, own large amounts of assets in Shanghai. Therefore, they have re-hired lawyer Zhang Baotang, collected evidence, and filed lawsuits against the shareholders. It is heard that a judgment has been made, ordering the shareholders to jointly repay Chen Xiuji and others' deposits of more than 8,000 yuan and interest.

Incoming Correspondence: Which Policy Should China Adopt to Deal with World Changes? (Continued)

Lecture by Zhang Yuanruo (Notes by Li Guangteng)

Some people may think that my theory is impossible, but I can say with certainty that this is not just a theory, it is indeed a current trend. It is not an overly optimistic fantasy, but an extremely possible conjecture. Anyone who understands the current world situation and is familiar with the national conditions of Japan will have the same view. If we want to defeat Japan, we must first know ourselves and our enemy, and we must understand Japan's position and have insight into their psychology in order to be successful. Although Japan is extremely aggressive towards China, they have long anticipated the crisis of 1936, and they are indeed afraid of the arrival of this crisis and regard it as the most serious national crisis. They are exactly what is called "outwardly strong but inwardly weak." Recently, the Japanese military department published a booklet, "The Essence of National Defense and its Strengthening," which contains the same panic as I have described. It can be seen that this is not just my personal prejudice. Therefore, they are now actively engaged in defeating the united front of China, Russia, the United States, and Britain, and are urgently working to prevent Russia and unite with the United States and Britain. (Regarding this point, it is a specialized issue. Today, I will only briefly explain how Japan is currently using all its ingenuity to sow discord, isolate China, and achieve its desires. Details will be discussed separately.) Therefore, now that we are in this time of urgent crisis, whether we can safely overcome the difficulties depends entirely on whether we can implement my proposal and my strategy. This is definitely something that can be predicted.

Speaking of the diplomatic status between China and Japan, our country is inherently superior to Japan. However, we cannot analyze the international situation and do not use the opportunities that are favorable to us, so that although our country's status is superior, we cannot obtain any benefits. Japan's status is isolated, but because they are good at utilizing it, they are actually superior to our country. This is a very worrying thing. If our government authorities can earnestly formulate a plan based on the principles I have talked about today and implement it diligently, I think it will definitely be effective. We must know that in international diplomacy, there is no right or wrong, no emotion, no chastity, no justice. What exists is only interest. What dominates the entire world situation is economics. (I published a book "Economic Observation of International Problems" in Minzhi Bookstore before, which explains it in detail, please refer to it.) What determines a country's diplomatic strategy is also economics and interests. From the above discussion, we have clearly understood that our country is currently in an extremely dangerous period. If we want to break this crisis, we must thoroughly understand the world situation and the actual interests of various countries in order to determine our diplomatic strategy. We must use it based on interests and obtain a favorable diplomatic position. All naive alliances and disconnections are inherently naive, and all false courtesy and connections are especially futile. (D) The response policies I mentioned earlier are actually only temporary solutions. When it comes to fundamental solutions, the first is that the people of the whole country can [rely on themselves]. I have recently advocated [self-reliance doctrine, which was published in Shenxin Shishi and other newspapers in October and November of this year]. Why do I say this? Because diplomacy only talks about interests. If we have no power, how can the great powers be willing to form alliances and connections with us? Therefore, fundamentally, we must cultivate our own strength so that they will look up to us and unite with us. This is the most basic condition and the fundamental principle for saving the country, surviving, and revitalizing the nation. (End)

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team Captures a Female Bandit on the Xin Ningshao Steamer

The Bandit is only in Her Twenties and Fashionably Dressed

A Handgun and Bullets Were Found in Her Suitcase

Her Testimony is Incoherent and She Has Been Handed Over to the Public Security Bureau

The Xin Ningshao steamer, operated by the Ningshao Company in this city, which runs the Shanghai-Ningbo line, set sail from Shanghai to Ningbo on the 10th of this month. At 5:00 PM that afternoon, when the ship was about to set sail, a young female bandit carrying weapons was captured by the police officers of the Municipal Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team in cabin 62 of the ship. After an interrogation by the Water Patrol General Team, she has now been handed over to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for disposition. A Datong News Agency reporter has investigated and reported the details below.

The Female Passenger Looked Flustered

The Xin Ningshao steamer was preparing to sail from Shanghai to Ningbo on the afternoon of the 10th. At around 3:00 PM, a young female passenger booked cabin 62 with Zhang Jinzhong, a waiter on the ship. After placing her small mesh basket, clothing bag, and fruit in the cabin, she went ashore because it was still early before the ship sailed. At about 5:00 PM, the female passenger returned with a small leather suitcase. When she was about to board the ship at the lower station pier, she was spotted by Li Yunting, a police officer of the Water Patrol Team, who noticed that she looked quite flustered.

A Handgun was Found in Her Suitcase

The police officer immediately joined the ship's escort police and followed her into cabin 62 for inspection. When they inspected her small leather suitcase, the female passenger suddenly claimed that she had forgotten the key at home. After speaking, she immediately got up and tried to escape. The police officers stopped her and found the key on her person. They opened the suitcase and found a handgun with the number 241560, and two rows of bullets, each row with eight bullets, a total of sixteen bullets. When the female passenger saw that her actions had been exposed, she immediately took out a gold bracelet and two finger rings and offered them as bribes to avoid further investigation. The police officers refused and placed her under guard.

A Thorough Search of the Ship's Cabins

The shipowner, upon hearing the news, feared that there were still accomplices hiding, and immediately ordered all the escort police officers to conduct a detailed inspection of the luggage and belongings of passengers in each cabin. No other contraband was found. The female bandit, along with her luggage and prohibited items, was escorted by the water police officer Li Yunting to the Dongjiadu Water Patrol General Team for investigation. Therefore, the ship's departure from the Bund was delayed until after 6:00 PM, more than an hour later than the usual departure time.

The Female Bandit's Testimony is Incoherent

After the female bandit was escorted to the Water Patrol General Team, she was strictly interrogated by the General Team Leader, Mr. Zhu Haishan. She has now been handed over to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for disposition. Her testimony at the Water Patrol Team is recorded below. Wu Zhangshi, 24 years old, from Ningbo, her husband is called Wu Wenpei, from Anhui, working as a coppersmith in France, location unknown. The handgun belongs to my husband's friend called Sun Ruifu, with a leather suitcase, entrusted me to take it to his home in Zhoushan, Ningbo. He is going to Zhuangyuan Bridge in Zhoushan. I have no place in Shanghai. My uncle runs the Ruichang Machine Factory on Tongzhou Road. I don't know there are handguns in the suitcase, etc.

The Evidence is Very Valuable

The evidence seized was also sent by the team to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for safekeeping. The list of evidence is as follows: two mesh baskets, one bundle, one leather suitcase, one handgun, sixteen bullets, two bullet clips, one pair of gemstone gold earrings, one gold bracelet, two gold rings, two gemstone rings, eighty yuan in banknotes (including one five-yuan counterfeit banknote from the Central Bank), one cigarette case, two baskets of fruit.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Sixth Chapter: A Poor Girl Does Not Feel Ashamed to Teach, Viewing Western Teachers as Unworthy of Respect, Vainly Humiliating One's Mind

Jia Duocai also knew that Aunt Hu herself felt embarrassed; she was just making conversation. He pointed to the square stool near the door and said to her, "Just sit here." After speaking, he smiled and said to Yueying, "There, there's a chair here, sit down." As he spoke, he gestured with his mouth towards the corner of the wall. Clearly, he had a different attitude towards Yueying. Yueying felt even more embarrassed by his appearance, and just lowered her head and fiddled with her buttons. Aunt Hu had already sat down, but seeing that she still looked embarrassed, she stood up again, grabbed Yueying's sleeve, and dragged her towards the empty chair over there, laughing, "At home, you can say anything, why don't you say a word here?" Yueying couldn't very well stand there stiffly, so she followed her gesture and sat down on the empty chair here. She was still smiling slightly, without uttering a word in reply. Jia Duocai also had considerable experience with matters of love and pleasure. But the people he had encountered were all people of that world, and they laughed and talked along with him. Now that he had encountered this girl from the countryside, who kept getting embarrassed, the situation became more and more awkward. As a result, he felt helpless. He put a cigarette in his mouth, put his hands behind his back, and paced back and forth in the room. He glanced at Yueying, constantly puffing out smoke. At this time, Yueying found the time to observe the room: the bedsheet on the opposite bed was the first thing that surprised her. The white background was as white as clouds, and the red flowers printed on it were as big as washbasins. Not to mention that, she looked closely for a long time but couldn't see any stitches on the bedsheet; it was a whole piece. Looking at the bottom of the bedsheet, it was very thick and substantial. She wondered how much cotton or felt was padded underneath. But looking at the quilt on top, there were three layers: the bottom layer was made of patterned silk, the middle layer was made of yellow silk, and the top layer was made of green silk. (89)

Zhang Xiaozi

— Qing Qu

Zhang Xiaozi is from Jiangbei. He built two thatched sheds in the corner of our Jiading West City to shelter from the wind and rain. Speaking of which, his life is spent pulling a rickshaw. Well then, who would bother to look at such a lowly person? However, his name [Zhang Xiaozi] is really not easy to come by—because everyone knows him. He is Zhang Xiaozi, but in fact, among his fellow villagers, he is clearly called Zhang Xiaozhi. One day, I didn't quite understand, so I got the reason from a fruit seller. He is extremely filial to his old mother, so no one among his fellow villagers doesn't call him Zhang Xiaozhi. But the character [孝] (filial piety) sounds almost like the character [小] (small), so that many people don't quite understand that he is a very respectable and commendable person in modern society!

It is said that his old mother is already over sixty years old, her eyes are blind, and she is extremely frail. His wife, a certain woman, does laundry for others at home and is not like the women of poor families, but she is respectful and obedient. They only have one son, who is just four years old. His family, old and young, barely manage to make a living, relying solely on him and his wife, one using two legs and the other using two hands to survive. Alas! Unexpectedly, one day, Zhang broke his kneecap, and as a result, he could no longer pull the rickshaw. As a result, he couldn't continue to cook, and there was no way to start a fire. His wife, with only ten fingers left, could also think of nothing. Watching his old mother sitting on the bed, fainting many times because she hadn't had a bite to eat for several days, Zhang couldn't help but shed tears and secretly said to his wife: [My old mother's life is coming to an end, what should we do? His wife replied: [How can I bear to watch her? Now there is only one solution, I don't know if you will allow it? When asked, his wife said with tears in her eyes, [Alas! Rather than let our old mother linger and starve to death, leaving you with regrets for the rest of your life, why not sell this ignorant child to someone else, so that the grandson can prolong the grandmother's life? Isn't that a method of urgent rescue? So, the couple took their four-year-old son, got forty thousand cash, and sold him to a boatman of the same hometown outside the West Gate, as a temporary means of providing food and comfort. Later, Zhang's leg injury healed, and he continued to live by pulling the rickshaw. To this day, he still serves his old mother with utmost respect and reverence! Hey—Zhang Xiaozhi's name has since spread among the people of Jiangbei, but the character [孝] (filial piety) always sounds like the character [小] (small), so I recorded him as such. It can also be seen that the saying "In a village of ten households, there must be loyalty and trustworthiness, and within five steps, there must be fragrant grass" is indeed not an empty word.

Records of the Fragrant Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Although he never knew the heavy responsibilities that an emperor should bear, he did sit on the throne, so there was this small dragon robe.—The robe was made of yellow satin, and all around it, many flying dragons were embroidered with gold thread. The color was still very bright. When the Empress Dowager bent down, leaned over the box lid, and looked carefully, there seemed to be a light inside that reflected onto the Empress Dowager's face through the glass. For the sake of preserving her son's qualification to wear this dragon robe, not long after Xianfeng died, the Empress Dowager did take great risks and fight against the surrounding hostile environment. It was thanks to this fight that Her Old Highness was able to seize great power, look down upon the world, and become a rare female politician in history. Her original intention in fighting for the master of this small dragon robe eventually fulfilled herself. This undoubtedly amounts to failure!

We gathered around and carefully admired this yellow robe embroidered with golden dragons, and thus discovered that its collar was made of blue tribute satin, and there were several pearls the size of longans studded on it. Its magnificence was certainly extremely magnificent, but it was also very small! Judging from the size of this dragon robe, Tongzhi was indeed a very thin and weak child.

He seemed to have a special love for bronze objects. Therefore, many of them were collected here. Among them were a pair of small bronze drums, very exquisitely made. I think that if these drums were played by a skilled drummer, the beauty of their rhythm would be unmatched by any drum in the world. But their lives have also ended with their master. They will forever lie dormant in these ancient palaces without making a sound. (199)

Weariness of Life

— Yan BOGUANG

The trend of modern trends is to emphasize art in everything. Miss Wang, who lives across the street, graduated from a certain art school in Shanghai. Her parents cultivated her until she graduated from a specialized school, which can be considered fulfilling their responsibilities. Because her father only runs a small foreign grocery store, and supplying her with several thousand yuan of tuition and miscellaneous fees is already exhausting.

But Miss Wang, at the age of seventeen, began to advocate for celibacy in front of her parents. It turned out that from a young age, her parents had arranged an engagement for her with the Chen family. Now, she is dissatisfied with the Chen family having so much sinful money and raised a serious protest to her father, accusing him of why he sold her freedom and sovereignty to a monetary object. Can love be exchanged for money?

Alas! Her father is a small businessman, how can he be a match for her sharp tongue and cutting words? How could it not make her father shrink back?

But her father only knew how to roar and wave his fists. She finally succumbed to her father's strict authority and her mother's encouragement.

On a certain night not far from the wedding date, she committed suicide by taking poison! The suicide note only had the words [I am weary of life, goodbye!]. Her father was very saddened to see that she had committed suicide and regretted not having listened to her demands in the first place, leading to today!

However, the general public is still ridiculing her father, saying what a waste it was to have spent so much money, only to get an artistic euphemism for suicide! Weariness of life! But learned people still deeply regret her fate! She was only twenty-one years old this year.

— Yin Juan

Song of Begging for Relief

— (I am a Villager)

The abnormal development of the city reflects the decline of the countryside. The call for rural relief, despite its high-pitched singing, only sees rural funds becoming increasingly depleted; the unemployed in the countryside compete to squeeze into the city. There is the suffering of having no land to live on.

Du Gongbu is a great poet. But his wife and children can't avoid freezing and hunger. Modern writers, hiding in the city, in order to cater to the tastes of the upper classes, even songs directly speaking of the suffering of the people are rarely seen. I am a villager, and you discuss me learning a [fallen leaf cicada's song]:

[The city is fat, the countryside is thin;

The city is fragrant, the countryside is smelly;

The city is glamorous, the countryside is ugly;

The city has high buildings reaching the Milky Way; the countryside has ten houses, nine are dilapidated.

The city, the village women's clothes don't cover their elbows.

Those who complain in the city are abundant, who sees the countryside panting and complaining!

Better to be a city dog than a country person.

Alas, the call for rural relief rises into the clouds, but how much watery gruel has ever been had!)

Random Remarks

Fishermen's Life on Taihu Lake

— Ni Shanglong

Taihu Lake is a vast expanse of water in Jiangnan, spanning the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. It covers an area of over eight hundred li. Although its waters do not produce monstrous waves, there are some treacherous conditions. However, the lake is very rich in aquatic products. Consequently, there are many people who make a living by fishing nets, spending all year floating and living on the lake.

There are about fifty or sixty large fishing boats in the lake, each capable of hoisting seven sails. They have no engines and rely entirely on wind power for propulsion. The size of the boats is comparable to merchant ships traveling on the Yangtze River. The value of each boat is approximately ten thousand yuan. They generally do not dock on the shore. If the people on board want to go ashore, they must use sampans to cross over. Most of these boat people are either relatives or members of the same clan, so they share common interests and can all stay in contact with each other. When fishing, two boats line up side by side, each with one end of the net attached, and they hoist their sails, allowing the force of the wind to propel them forward. The fish caught are divided equally between the two boats, and there are no disputes over who has worked harder or less.

For the boats, the entire year's planning hinges on winter. When the north wind howls fiercely, they all beam with smiles, sharing their joy. This is because fish are hatched in the spring and grow large by winter, and in the extreme cold, they become numb and unable to move, mostly clinging to the mud to keep warm. The boat people take advantage of this time to drag mud nets, which requires little effort, and with the force of the gale, they move quickly forward, sometimes covering two or three hundred li in a night, catching three or four thousand catties of fish or more per day. However, what they worry about most is that although Taihu Lake is wide, it is very shallow. Often, when there is too much wind and snow, the lake water suddenly freezes into ice. In that case, the production they have earnestly hoped for throughout the year will be in vain.

Because of the above, they have a very rich experience in predicting the weather, and some of their predictions are very accurate. For example, this summer was very hot. According to those who are experienced on the lake: [There will definitely be very cold weather in winter.] Other observations include that if the ninth day of the third lunar month is fixed, there will undoubtedly be severe cold. The quicksand in the lake wells up and almost becomes lake "cream" (lake water freezing, which boat people colloquially call "cream"). Therefore, when they are sailing in cold weather and see quicksand welling up in the lake and the water viscous like a paste, and feel the boat moving sluggishly, they dip a pole into the water and drain it. If the water droplets drip with difficulty, then they know that the lake is about to "cream" and quickly sail the boat to a sunny mountainside with food supplies, waiting for the spring breeze to thaw the ice. They also know when the ice will thaw, and on what day the east wind or southeast wind will blow. They have a thorough understanding of the changes in sunny weather, rain, and wind, but mostly they can only predict them without understanding the reasons.

Every man and woman on the fishing boats loves to drink wine. This is their most common habit. Therefore, they must drink when they go ashore, and drink as much as possible. Even on the sampans that are used to purchase grain and other supplies, a wine bag is an indispensable adornment. Women and men are quite the opposite. They are all diligent and frugal, with absolutely no such habit. In addition to satisfying their hunger, they also knit nets and sew clothes. Because of the environment, there is not a single woman who does not understand needlework. When it is the cold weather fishing season, they stay up all night, helping the men raise and lower the nets.

Marriages on the boats, except for a few who marry residents on land, are mostly between people of the same kind. When the boat people go ashore to visit relatives, they must bring some dried or fresh fish and shrimp to give to their relatives, but the relatives must also reciprocate with some other gifts. If they do not, they are considered to be looking down on them, and many break off relations because of this. When children get married, the parents of the bride and groom must give each other fifty or sixty catties of New Year cake at the end of the year. Therefore, families with many relatives often have to make more than five or six hundred catties of New Year cake. This is also a strange custom.

There is also education on the boats, but their textbooks are only a few copies of the "Hundred Family Surnames," "Three Character Classic," "Thousand Character Classic," "Prodigy Poems," and so on. The teaching method is the same as that of a private tutor, entirely individualized. The teacher is hired by a dozen or so boats, and their meals and lodging are provided. The cost is shared depending on the number of children from each boat. They treat the teacher with great respect. In addition to the three meals, they also provide snacks in the afternoon, which are exclusively for the teacher. Every two or three days, they hold a separate banquet to entertain the teacher. In addition, the students' families take care of the teacher's laundry, sewing, making the bed, folding the blankets, and cleaning the water pipe. The students take care of this, so the teacher does not have to worry about it. However, the tuition is very low, only fifty or sixty yuan per year.

The above information was all told to me by my old friend (a native of Dongshan, Taihu Lake), and I have written it down.

Selection of Exhibits for Chinese Art Exhibition

The International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London is scheduled to open in London in November next year. The Chinese exhibits have been selected and appraised by a preparatory committee of the exhibition, which has invited experts Yang Zhensheng, Ye Gongchuo, and more than ten others to participate. The main parts of the exhibits are calligraphy, painting, bronze, and porcelain. It is reported that in terms of calligraphy and painting, more than 300 pieces have been selected, ranging from the Qianlong and Kangxi periods of the former Qing Dynasty to the Five Dynasties and Song Dynasty. In terms of porcelain, more than 300 pieces have also been selected from the Qing Dynasty and earlier. However, due to standards, only more than 180 pieces of bronze ware from the Three Dynasties have been selected. A preliminary exhibition is planned to be held in Shanghai in March of next spring. At that time, foreigners will be invited to offer opinions and request modifications. As long as China does not experience any difficulties or cause the exhibits to be difficult to transport and display, temporary adjustments can be made. After participating in the London exhibition, when the exhibits return to China, they will be exhibited again in Nanjing.

Director Ding of the Chinese College at the University of Frankfurt Arrives in Nanjing

Requests Allocation of Sponsorship Funds

The Chinese College at the University of Frankfurt, Germany, was founded by Professor Richard Wilhelm, who once taught at Peking University. Countess Graefin Sierstorpff of Germany donated to help establish it. Wilhelm was a specialist in Chinese Confucianism and translated the Four Books and Five Classics, as well as the books of Lao Tzu, Zhuangzi, Mozi, and Liezi, introducing many Chinese philosophies to Europeans for study. After the European War, when Germany's economy was in difficulty, Wilhelm painstakingly maintained the Chinese College, which was not affected. Wilhelm died the year before last, and the successor Director is D. Rousselle. The Vice Director is Ding Wenjiang's younger brother, Mr. Ding Wenyuan, who consulted with our country's envoy Jiang Zuobin. Upon proposal by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the central government and its passing, China would sponsor 80,000 marks annually as the Chinese Lecture Fund for the University of Frankfurt. However, due to financial difficulties, it was subsequently resolved that the Ministry of Finance would allocate 40,000 yuan. The Ministry of Education, on the other hand, was already allocating 5,000 yuan annually to the college for publishing the journal "Sinica." Now, the subsidy for the journal has been allocated during Minister Wang Shijie's term, but the 40,000 yuan from the Ministry of Finance has not yet been remitted. The Vice Director of the college, Ding Wenyuan, came to China specifically for this matter. He arrived at the Ministry of Education at 4:00 PM on the 12th and consulted with Department Chief Qiu and Section Chief Zheng to request the allocation of funds. It was mentioned that the college is now planning to establish a Chinese Culture Museum and that it has been in contact with intermediaries in Shanghai. Several thousand yuan has already been donated, and there have also been donations for the museum, which will be established soon. It is hoped that the 40,000 yuan from the Ministry of Finance will be allocated quickly to facilitate the progress of the Chinese lecture project. He is currently consulting with the Ministry of Finance on the remittance. He also said that the college has a board of directors, whose chairman is the envoy to China, Bu Liangxi.

Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Institute Sends Letters to Schools Nationwide to Investigate Agriculture, Forestry, and Economics

Fill Out Survey Forms and Receive a Free Subscription to the "Current Affairs Monthly"

Pay Attention to Facts and Avoid Misleading Information When Conducting Surveys

The Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Institute sent letters to schools nationwide yesterday, stating: "We are writing to inform you that, for the purpose of studying agricultural, forestry, and economic issues in our country, our institute has formulated a survey form on the population density of rural forests and land utilization. We have sent letters to various schools recommended by the county governments or education bureaus to fill out the forms. We are grateful for the enthusiastic support of teachers and staff from various schools. Many schools have already filled out the survey forms, but a small number of schools have not yet filled them out, presumably because the survey forms did not reach them. According to statistical principles, the more locations surveyed, the closer the results are to the truth. Our institute wants the results to be as close to the truth as possible, so we are sending another copy each of the survey forms on the population density of rural forests and land utilization, the second survey form on the tenancy system, and the survey form on the food problem, along with postage stamps for returning them. Please distribute and fill out the survey forms and return them to our institute. Once we receive the filled out survey forms, we will send you a free one-month subscription to the 'Current Affairs Monthly.' If you are willing to continue working as a correspondent for our institute, we will gradually send you subscriptions to the 'Current Affairs Monthly' or other publications after our review and approval. If there are no teachers or staff at your school who are familiar with rural conditions, please forward the forms to enthusiastic individuals in the local rural areas who are dedicated to public service to fill them out. All the questions in the survey forms are simple, and anyone familiar with agricultural and forestry conditions can report them. However, if you are not careful when filling them out, it is easy to stray too far from the truth. Therefore, we would like to ask you to pay attention to the actual facts when filling them out. Please take note of this and handle accordingly. We would be very grateful."

1,159,306 Visitors

The municipal zoo on Wenmiao Road in the Southern District covers an area of ​​7.3 mu. Since its opening on August 1 of last year, up to June 30 of this year, a total of eleven months, excluding holidays when it is closed, it has been open for a total of 280 days. The total number of visitors was 1,159,306, with an average of approximately 4,000 visitors per day. The day with the most visitors was National Day, with a total of 13,730 visitors. The day with the fewest visitors was December 7, with 594 visitors, due to the extremely cold weather and heavy rain. In general, the number of visitors to the zoo has not decreased since it opened, which shows that the facilities of the zoo are really in great demand. Sports News: The Finnish Sports Association Establishes a School for Athletes

▲ Well-equipped and Inexpensive

▲ Long-distance Runner Nurmi Appointed as Instructor

A Groundbreaking Initiative in the World of Sports

(Reuters, London) The Finnish Sports Association, to cultivate athletic talent, plans to establish an academy for athletes, a pioneering initiative in the world of sports. Sports teachers, athletic instructors, and those aspiring to be athletes can enter the school at minimal cost for specialized training. The Finnish Sports Association's planned athlete school, located in Virikkilä, southern Finland, is nearing completion. The six-story building can accommodate two hundred students. Its facilities include a gym, tennis court, dormitory, dining hall, reading room, smoking room, lecture hall, and library. The 34-acre grounds feature a running track, athletic field, tennis court, and soccer field. In winter, there will be a skating hill and ice rink. Funding comes from public subsidies, donations, the sale of lottery tickets, and concerts. World-renowned long-distance runner Nurmi personally planned the track and will also serve as an instructor. A resident physician will be stationed at the school. Aspiring athletes who volunteer to enter the school for training need only pay two shillings per day, which includes tuition, board, and lodging. According to the Finnish Sports Association, this is a world first, and many other countries will likely follow suit.

Western League Football This Week

Referee Assignments
