Free Talk

The Faithfulness and Elegance of Translation

— Shuang Jie

The famous modern Italian aesthetician, Croce (B. Croce), said in his book on aesthetics: [What has been created in a beautiful form, we can re-express it in a logical form, but what already has a beautiful form cannot be changed into another form that is also beautiful. The result of translation is either a reduction and damage to the original expression, or putting the original expression into a melting pot and mixing it with the translator's own impressions, creating a new expression... The saying "a faithful ugly woman or an unfaithful beauty" perfectly illustrates the dilemma of every translator.] What he means is that if we are not satisfied with simply interpreting the original text when translating, but further demand an expression that is as beautiful as the original, we will find ourselves in a dilemma. This view, to anyone who has had even a little translation experience, will not find it an exaggeration. The creation and development of a nation's language and writing is determined by its most fundamental economic life. If the economic nature is different, the national psychology and the cultural state that reflects this psychology will naturally have different appearances. It is already not easy to understand the art of another country, let alone express it with aesthetic words [appropriately]!

When an author is in the midst of a strong artistic impulse, the value of that beauty is complete. When that impulse forms a clear concept in the brain, that value is reduced by one point. When the concept is translated into formed words and entrusted to the arm and written out, that value is reduced by another point, but that is only its original appearance. When a translator from another country uses a mind cultivated in different living habits to understand it, experience it, and then express it in another language through language and obscurity, it is already very far from the original author's intention. If the translator has a deep understanding of the original author's temperament, living environment, and the language they use, and can freely use their own language, this can still give the reader a glimpse of the rough outline of the original work, otherwise it will be a hundred thousand miles away from the original. Moreover, a word does not exist in isolation. Hidden behind the word is the entire vertical history and horizontal range of that nation. What is the connotation of a certain word in the vocabulary of that country, and what kind of associations does it evoke in people's minds? All of these must be given a clear analysis. From this point of view, the work of translation, even if it is not as impossible as Croce says, is at least very laborious, very difficult, and should be approached with caution.

The French critic Guyau said: [The ideal straight line is the shortest distance from one point to another, and the ideal style is also the shortest distance from one person's mood to another person's mood.] Starting from this mathematical and mechanical concept, Spencer said that language is a machine for people to communicate with each other. Finding a word's position properly to evoke the reader's mood is a matter of using intuition and perception to evoke or guide attention and association. This is also true in translation. Constantly dissolving, refining, and embellishing, to seek a forced resemblance between two languages, reducing the distance between them to the smallest possible limit, is the responsibility of the translator, and when he has done so, he has perfectly completed his task.

Since the publication of the special translation issue of literary magazines, there have been two publications, Translation and Folk Literature, that specialize in introducing foreign literature. In the sense of [attacking flaws with the help of others], translated works from abroad are only considered too few, not too many. However, what we require is good translation. Even if we cannot have someone like Aylmer Maude who accompanied Tolstoy in Russia for many years before starting to translate his works, we still cannot take this work too lightly, hoping to introduce foreign works by holding a pen in one hand and flipping through a dictionary in the other. Our requirements for current translators can be written in a long essay if we say too much, but in short, it is just a little hope that the translation is [on the one hand, faithful to the original author, and on the other hand, fluent for the reader.]

A Glimpse of Tokyo

— Li Qiao

Sitting in the train, feeling bored, occasionally looking out the window: Under the azure sky is a vast expanse of fields, ancient farmhouses, half-hidden in the verdant woods, with only a hazy cloud of smoke at the horizon, shrouded with a few faint distant trees.

This vast territory of Annam is enough for the train to run. I got up at six o'clock in the morning, and I've been traveling continuously, but the destination is still far away.

The weather is particularly hot. We who grew up in temperate regions find this climate exceptionally difficult to bear. In addition, the unpleasant, miasmic smell I encountered in Haiphong constantly follows and attacks me, causing a bit of a headache.

Almost all of the passengers on the train are Annamese people with teeth dyed jet black, chewing mouthfuls of bright red betel nut. Among these people, there are a few aristocrats wearing short black gauze robes, white cloth pants, a gauze turban wrapped around their heads, and only a pair of wooden shoes on their feet, without socks. Apart from these few people, most of them are poorly dressed, coffee-colored gowns, unkempt, and unclean working class people.

These laborers who have come out of the countryside carry all sorts of agricultural products they have worked hard to obtain, sitting crowded and noisy on the train, probably taking things to the city to sell? They look so excited, some even put their feet on the seats, chattering and conversing with their companions, making the train very lively.

Burying my head, feeling quite bored, I leaned on the train window, and my heart couldn't help but think of my father far away in the heavens, my old and helpless father. At this time, he might be gripping a hoe and digging the ground... But how could he have thought that at this moment, his son, whom he was eagerly hoping would come to help him, would quietly leave him? And, this is a departure with not a penny to be had...

As I thought silently, my heart couldn't help but feel a little heavy, but it was immediately encouraged by the vague hope for the future, and I felt somewhat relieved again.

It was already late, and I don't know when many of the passengers had gotten off the train, leaving only a few in the car. Dusk brought a cool river breeze, and in the dim twilight, the majestic buildings of Tokyo could already be seen dimly. A twilight haze like cooking smoke permeated the surroundings, the train gave two long whistles, and then rumbled onto that iron bridge that shone with the civilization of the twentieth century, about eight or nine miles long, spanning the Red River and the Clear River.

This bridge is about four zhang wide. Cars can pass on both sides of the tracks. Under the bridge is the rushing river water, and many wooden rafts float on the river, reflecting the bright electric lights of Tokyo. The scenery on this river is particularly beautiful!

Sitting on the train, it took about ten or twenty minutes to cross the bridge. The bridge leads directly to Tokyo Station. After the train crossed the Red River and the Clear River, it passed over many houses in Tokyo. Looking out the window, the houses below the bridge were so low that they were almost hidden under the train.

When the train arrived in Tokyo, it was already the time when the lights were coming on. The stores on both sides of the road displayed dazzling goods, and cars roared on the smooth asphalt road, speeding past like lightning. Needless to say, this emerging colonial city is like other modern metropolises.

Carrying my luggage out of the train, I went to a store opened by a Cantonese person, where I had a meal, and then hurriedly jumped back onto the car.

At this time, it was already past nine o'clock at night. In this night where only the river breeze was whistling, carrying a heart of reluctant farewell, I parted ways with Tokyo!

On the Relationship Between Works and Life

— Zhou Yuying

Recently, Mr. Lin Huanping, Mr. Wu Liping, and Mr. Meng Jia have successively discussed the issue of writers' real lives. Mr. Lin advocates that writers should have [rich] [life experiences]. Mr. Wu says that [writers are by no means created, they are only people who actually live, and their works are only direct life experiences. They do not live in order to produce great works]. Mr. Meng supports the former and opposes the latter. I would like to say a few points on this issue, and if the debate does not stop here, it may be good for everyone to use as a reference.

First, literature is ultimately a discipline centered on emotion. It was not until the emergence of modern and progressive literature that the element of thought was added, and then emotion and thought were given equal importance. However, no matter how much the thought in literature is elevated, the expression of emotion and thought in literature still relies on [imagination]. Imagination constitutes the substance of literature, and it expresses fervent emotion – emotion that passes through a certain thought. Since the substance of literature is constituted by imagination, imagination only has the distinction between deep and mellow and superficial and poor, and there is absolutely no distinction between abundant or not abundant life. Homer's poems, Tolstoy's novels, it would probably be an unreasonable request to ask them to taste the life depicted in their works before engaging in creation.

Second, perhaps many of Balzac's and Gorky's works are [records of their actual lives lived through]. But there are many actual lives of poverty, wandering, and labor like those of Balzac and Gorky in the world. Why is it that only Balzac and Gorky were able to write works? Also, people like Ye Shaojun, Mao Dun, and Zhang Tianyi in China are by no means absolutely failed writers. Should all of their works be records of actual life? At the same time, if Balzac and Gorky used their strong artistic ability of imagination to depict other stories, such as Sinclair's depiction of the destruction of an oil tycoon, and the misery of coal mines and slaughterhouses, wouldn't this have the same value as a record of private life?

Third, literature is a substance constituted by artistic imagination. The constitution of this imagination does not necessarily have to be limited to the scope of personal actual life, but it is not difficult for imagination to depart from the general life of reality. If a writer writes a work with a certain purpose, and does not have such an experience in his own actual life, he must imagine social matters in a pavilion or a western-style building. A person with strong imagination can write a work that seems to have actually happened, but a person with immature imagination can only say stupidly and untruthfully, and the work completely loses its authenticity. Therefore, I believe that the success or failure of a work is entirely a matter of the writer's ability. Although a writer with weak ability may find it easier to succeed in describing stories that he has experienced, this is the writer's trick and cannot generalize the whole of literature.

From History to Astronomy

— Prism

Recently, astronomy has gradually attracted attention. The only relatively complete existing book on astronomy is often mentioned; the terminology of astronomy compiled by the National Institute for Compilation and Translation has even appeared before the terminology of physics; a illustrated book about constellations has also appeared; over a dozen books on astronomy are planned to be included in the second collection of the Wan Qian Library. Individual bookstores have also printed some works on the physics of the universe, the mysterious universe, and pilgrimages to the starry sky, etc.

I myself am also very happy to be reading astronomy books, which naturally brings me joy. In the past, when looking for astronomy books, I felt a bit of distress. I couldn't find many astronomy books in the few libraries I could go to. I wanted to buy them myself, but I never had enough money, and some were terribly expensive. For example, the original version of "Pilgrimage to the Starry Sky," a thin book of just over ninety pages, cost four and a half yuan. Moreover, when I occasionally had some spare money, the bookstore might not have the books I wanted, such as the astronomical almanac. Since the cessation of publication of the Chinese Astronomical Almanac in 1933, I had to buy the English-language "Nautical Almanac" that year, and the Japanese Astronomical Almanac in another year. A few days ago, when I went to buy the astronomical almanac, the new ones hadn't arrived yet, but I happened to see the British abridged "Nautical Almanac" in a nautical supply store, so I bought it to read.

The nautical almanac is practical, so it naturally omits some things that can be considered unimportant. For example, the section on planetary movements only mentions Venus, Mars, Jupiter, and Saturn, but not Mercury, Uranus, or Neptune. This reminded me of someone's opinion that Uranus and Neptune are irrelevant to society. I believe that opinion, although if there were a book specifically about Uranus and Neptune, I would very much like to read it, but that is just a personal preference.

However, I must state that this preference is not for the sake of increasing astronomical knowledge. My occasional exposure to this field has not made me so foolish as to think that I can specialize in Uranus and Neptune. However, I know that Lowell spent his life studying Mars, and although he was very specialized, the books he wrote were quite sufficient to provide material for strange discussions, and everyone was quite happy to know a little bit. In the past two years, it seems that Jupiter, rather than Mars, has attracted more attention. According to the opinions of those who believe in the "two stars meet" theory, Jupiter is the key to the formation of the solar system. The history of the sun may be recorded on planets beyond Saturn, so perhaps Uranus and Neptune will one day become a common topic for ordinary people.

Ten years ago, Laplace's nebular hypothesis was still widely believed. I also read a small booklet called "From Nebula to Mankind" and seemed to have gained some understanding. But now, the contradictions between astronomy and geography implicit in this kind of theory that connects astronomy and geography have finally been discovered. The age of the sun's formation measured by the nebular hypothesis is not sufficient for the formation of the earth, let alone the development of life on earth.

Recent historians no longer confine themselves to historical facts after the existence of language and writing, but extend the timeline, some even starting from protozoa. If this is said to be the progress of history, this progress depends on the progress of other sciences as a foundation. The study of ancient societies requires the study of anthropology to have some direction, and anthropology itself has many questions that are geological questions, which lead to the entire problem of the earth, and earth science is only a branch of astronomy. Just from the fact that astronomy has not yet been able to determine the age of the earth, the extension of the historical timeline can only reach a certain limit, and even within this limit, there are not necessarily no problems.

It is natural for humans to place themselves at the center of everything, but this has given great obstacles to the theory of evolution in the past, and even now ordinary schools are unwilling to broaden the boundaries of history. However, those who know the importance of evolution to history may think it absurd to drag history into astronomy. But I believe that under the topic "From Nebula to Mankind," there will always be new and good books appearing.

Tomorrow (10)(6)

— Written by (Joseph Conrad), translated by Wu Xiangyu

Her headscarf fell to the ground, and he bent down to pick it up; she was gone. He wrapped it around his arm and walked boldly towards the window. He saw a burly fat man sitting in an armchair, an unshaded lamp, and a large, flat face with shaggy hair all around, with a wide mouth yawning; he also saw Miss Bessan's head and upper body. The yelling had stopped; the blind man had achieved his goal. He thought that everything was unsatisfactory, and his heart was extremely chaotic. His father was crazy; he couldn't go into the house. He had no money to go back, and a hungry partner left in London might be starting to think that he had been deliberately ignored. ["Damn it,"] he murmured. Of course, he could open the door and go in; but they might tie him up so tightly that he couldn't breathe just because he didn't ask; this was not a big deal, but he was extremely afraid of being locked up, even by mistake. He felt cold all over as he thought of this place, and he stomped heavily on the wet grass.

["What are you doing? -- A sailor?"] An excited voice said.

She had run out, and it was just a black shadow, a shadow attracted by the reckless shadow waiting for her at her window. ["Anything. My talents are not limited to being a sailor on a ship. This time, I came home that way."]

["Where did you come back from?"] she asked.

["After a happy banquet,"] he said, ["coming on the London train -- do you know? Huh? I hate being closed in a train. I don't feel so bad about a house."]

["Ah,"] she said, ["that's lucky."]

["Because in a house, you can open that damn door at any time and run onto the road in front of you."]

["From now on, won't you come back?"]

["At least not for sixteen years,"] he laughed. ["To this rabbit hole, eating a bad shovel..."]

["A ship isn't that big either."] she said sarcastically.

["No, but the sea is big."]

She lowered her head, as if her ears were drawn to the sound of the world, and she heard the tide stirred up by yesterday's sea breeze beyond the seawall, slapping the shore, making a monotonous, solemn vibration, as if the whole earth had become a funeral bell.

["Hey, that's what they call a ship a ship. You love her, you leave; a sea voyage isn't a marriage."] He quoted a sailor's proverb so nonchalantly.

["That's not a marriage,"] she whispered.

["What is your purpose in coming here?"] she asked fearfully.

["Five pounds,"] he replied immediately. ["We enjoyed ourselves a little too much and got into some trouble."]

["Have you been drinking all the time?"] she asked.

["Drunk for three days; deliberately so. I am not addicted to alcohol -- don't get me wrong. Nothing, and no one, can subdue me unless I want to. I can be as firm as a rock. My partner saw the newspaper this morning, and he said to me: [Go ahead, Harry: love your father. You can definitely get five pounds]. So we scraped together the fare from everyone's pockets. A cursed mockery."]

Finance Supply and Demand are on a Balanced Line

Gold Price Shows No Significant Fluctuations

Slight Increase and Slight Decrease...Return Hanging Two Jiao

Since the gold market rebounded the day before yesterday, the situation has been stable. The market initially rose and then fell yesterday. Although the result was a slight decrease, the day's market conditions were very mediocre, and sentiment was very stable. Supply and demand are balanced, lacking special risks. The morning opening showed that both British and American silver markets were shrinking overseas, and the forward silver price was flat. However, large-scale capital was relatively strong, exchange rates slightly contracted, and London spot gold rose by half a penny. Pre-market trading opened outside the exchange, immediately rising to 71.2 yuan. Sentiment was quite stable. Subsequently, the Central Bank's listing was announced, with both British and American rates remaining flat, and the customs gold unit rose by one li. The standard gold price was listed at 1003.5 yuan and continued to rise. The morning opening was high, and the situation was stable after the opening, hovering around 2 yuan. Then, the bank's support for the shilling caused buying to rise in the market, leading to an increase. Knowing that HSBC's British and American exchange rates would not change, supply became abundant, and the market was downstream. Banks heavily sold US dollars, and sellers showed strength, once approaching the 70 yuan mark. However, because the Central Bank supported the shilling, the price fell but recovered. The silver balance tax was announced unchanged, still levied at 6.75%. The British exchange rate, calculated at 1 shilling, 5 pence, and 59375, was even flatter, fluctuating between 1 and 2 yuan, but the trend was easier to pull up. Therefore, buying activity slightly increased after entering the market, and the upward trend resumed, causing the 10 yuan line to turn around. However, many people took the opportunity to sell, and banks continued to sell US dollars, suddenly reviving the buying sentiment. The price fell immediately after rising, but the overall trend was still fluctuating at noon. The market continued to be stable in the afternoon, and trading was normal, with a sluggish market for quite some time. Until the first report from Mumbai showed a decrease of 4.4.4 anna, the market price rose, but the selling sentiment followed. Banks slightly sold US dollars, and sellers took advantage of the situation to become active, gradually moving downstream. When the 70 yuan mark was broken, many long positions rushed to sell, and large accounts also cut their losses. Sentiment was uneasy, leading to a decline. However, because the exchange market was normal and the second report from Mumbai showed no change, buyers repeatedly became active at low prices, and silver bars were also digested, gradually rising back to over 7 yuan. However, the upward momentum was only temporary, and large accounts still closed positions. The market finally succumbed within the 70 yuan mark, which was due to the swap relationship, and many long positions dared not linger. The current swap period coincides with Saturday, starting early at 10 am. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was 972.7 yuan, an increase of 2.7 yuan compared to the previous close. The situation was ambiguous at the beginning, but due to Shunmao, Richang, and Wanxing selling bars, the price retreated from 3 yuan to 1.5 yuan. Hengyu, Fuxing, Yongda, and Decheng accepted bars, rising to 2.5 yuan. Shenkang and Fuyu sold, retreating again to 1.4 yuan. At this time, Zhengjin was selling spot shillings at 9375, while HSBC and Citibank were supporting, stabilizing sentiment. Dadecheng, Fuxing, Yongzhaofeng, Changyongfeng, Yuanchang, and Yongfu'an accepted bars at low prices, gradually rising to 4 yuan. Knowing that HSBC's British and American exchange rates would not change, Fuxing, Yongdingkang sold, dropping to 2.5 yuan. Huabi supported February shillings at 4375, and Dadecheng and Futaiheng still had buying interest, gradually rising to 3.5 yuan. Soon, Shanghai and others came out with February US dollars at 875, and Sassoon also had selling interest. Fuxing, Yongda, Dadecheng, Dingkang, Qingyu, etc. sold, falling to 0.1 yuan. The Central Bank supported January shillings at 625. Dadecheng and Fuxingyong maintained at low prices, gradually rising. The silver balance tax was announced unchanged. After this, the price once rose back to over 2 yuan. Shanghai came out with February US dollars at 875, and Hengyu supplied bars, falling again to 1 yuan. After entering the market, sentiment gradually strengthened. Fuyu, Dingkang, Juchang, Hengxingyuan, Yongli, etc. rushed to enter bars, rising to 4.5 yuan. Changda and Dalian Gang took the opportunity to sell bars at high prices, dropping to 3.3 yuan. However, Juchang, Fuxing, and Yuanyi continued to accept, and the price later rose to 4.5 yuan. Zhaofeng, Changda, Dalian Gang, Hengxingchang, Dada Xingyong, etc. successively sold off, and banks continued to sell US dollars. Sassoon sold light shillings, gradually moving downstream. Later, Tianfeng sold heavily, dropping to 1.2 yuan. Huixiang and Hongxing maintained at low prices, and Yuanmao Yong also came to buy, stabilizing the situation. The price then rose back to 2.2 yuan. Securities Bond Market in Extreme Stagnation

｜Continuing a Small Fraction of Five Cents, One Dime to Three Dimes｜

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, foreign exchange rates, and market prices remained almost unchanged. The stagnation was unprecedented, and most people were watching. Although those who are bullish recently feel it's a good deal, the money supply is ultimately a factor. For forward contracts, the market price is too high, and the spread is excessive. Although money is tight, it shouldn't affect the fundamentals of the bond market. The environment is good, the country is united, and there are many rescue methods being considered. The financial sector prefers shorting sterling to public bonds, which is also a business strategy, choosing to act for profit. Therefore, although the near and far terms are distorted, it is a temporary phenomenon. Before long, domestic cash will return, and it should not be difficult to gradually return to normal. Although it is unknown whether the large short positions in the market will cover their positions, retail investors' arbitrage trading has gradually picked up. Market prices may have a round of recovery. Because the accumulation of weakness has been going on for a long time, the highest price for the current June contract is already down a little over four yuan. A slight movement in trading can easily trigger short covering and new long positions. Yesterday, only the opening session in the morning saw a relatively large sell-off of contract number 38, and the market price remained sluggish, down a small two or three dimes. The second session and the opening and closing sessions in the afternoon immediately entered a state of abnormal stagnation. Silk and Tea - Sales of Chinese Silk to the US Have Been Completely Usurped by Japanese Silk

Japanese silk is being sold cheaply in the United States, causing sales of Chinese silk to the US to plummet. This year, from January to the end of last month (ie November), the total amount of silk shipped from Shanghai to the US was only 2,488 bales, only about two-tenths of the amount in the same period last year (over 12,000 bales of silk were exported to the US from January to the end of November last year). At the beginning of the month, US sales seemed to be active, and each US firm in Shanghai started to cover their short positions. For a time, over 700 bales of yellow and white silk were traded, and the price also rose by 30-40 yuan. However, the situation was only temporary. Yesterday, according to Mr. Shi, an important Chinese employee of the silk building of American firm Ganli Foreign Firm, the reason for the decline in sales of Chinese silk to the US is that Japanese Akiran, although it was a soft harvest this year, has a very large backlog of goods (raw silk) from previous years. They are now actively shipping and dumping in the US. Therefore, more than 40,000 bales of Japanese silk were imported into New York in the middle of last month, and the current inventory (Japanese silk) is about 70,000 bales. They are being sold cheaply in the market, and the process is continuing unabated. Therefore, the current silk market price is unlikely to stabilize, and there is still no possibility of a turnaround in sales of Chinese silk to the US.

Precious Eyebrow Pearl Tea Sales to Europe Recovered

Green tea such as the eyebrow shrimp eye sesame pearl of Luzhuang has been quiet in recent days. Yesterday, British firms Xiehe, Tongfu, Fushi, and Dude Foreign Firms responded to overseas telegraphs and gathered to search for it again. However, because there are not many high-quality ones, the goods of high-end firms are still in short supply. Green tea such as needle eyebrow and bud eyebrow also continue to be actively traded. Metals - White Iron Tile Was Almost Completely Purchased

Due to the shortage of white iron in the spring and summer seasons, the industry did not dare to place orders for the autumn and winter sales. Therefore, the current imports are like morning stars, and the inventory in the market is also about to be purchased completely. Currently, building gangs and product gangs are adding more, but the No. 26 color is already in a situation where there is no stock to supply. Driven by the environment, prices are rising step by step. It is estimated that No. 24 sells for 11 yuan 4 and a half dimes per dan, No. 26 sells for 12 yuan 5 dimes, and No. 28 sells for 13 yuan 3 and a half dimes, all up about 2 dimes compared to before. It is found that the current circulating goods are extremely scarce, and the morale is very good. Therefore, there is still a possibility that the standard will continue to rise.

Arrival of Small Guangzhou Leather, Market Weak

In the past month, the 2-foot, 6-foot, 18-sheet large Guangzhou leather has seen active purchasing and a brisk market trend. The standard price soared to 11 yuan 5 dimes. Because buyers were in urgent need, they did not reduce their demand because of the high price. Therefore, the market trading was still very pleasant. In recent days, the new goods have arrived frequently, but because the end of the year is approaching and money is tight, the way out is much less and the market is declining day by day. It is estimated that each dan sells for 10 yuan 2 and a half dimes, a drop of 5 dimes compared to before. If the decline continues to weaken, morale will soften again, and there is a fear of another drop in sales.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Humor of the League of Nations Council

— Niu

The weather was sultry, and I was sitting alone in my garret, feeling very bored. My body felt a little itchy. Thinking that I hadn't taken a bath in over a month, I decided to go take one. So I grabbed a change of clothes and went to a nearby bathhouse. I undressed, took off my belt, washed, scrubbed my back, got out of the tub, wiped myself dry—everything. The attendant was very kind and even placed a short stool in front of me before I went to sleep, to massage my feet. At that moment, my happiness and joy were truly beyond words. [I don't know if the ox dreams of being a butterfly, or the butterfly dreams of being an ox. There must be a distinction between the ox and the butterfly.]

At that time, I looked up at the ceiling, picked my teeth with a toothpick, or examined my fingernails, which I hadn't trimmed in over two months, to see how long they had grown. At this moment, I, Niu, was truly relaxed and carefree, pure and without worries, completely happy. If there were a camera at this moment, taking a picture of me in this [bull-headed horse] pose, I think it would be even more comical and humorous than the faces of [Laurel] and [Hardy].

A dispatch from Geneva on the 10th reported that when the League of Nations Council reopened its meeting this afternoon, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu spoke, severely criticizing Hungary. [He said that they had never felt such a loss as the death of Count Albert Apponyi, the former Hungarian representative to the League of Nations. The Count had always relied on this to engage in debate, and Hungarian commentators were now facing unwarranted condemnation. He had resided in England and Switzerland for a long time. Could one ask if the histories of these two countries allowed fugitives to carry weapons and practice with weapons, bullets, and explosives?] Many council members were uneasy upon hearing the Romanian Foreign Minister's words. The Italian representative, Aloisi, stared at the ceiling, the French Foreign Minister, Leygues, picked his teeth, and the British Lord Privy Seal, Eden, frequently examined his fingernails. I think the several council members of the League of Nations were somewhat distressed at this moment, because as members of the League of Nations Council, they were unable to resolve the problem of the Marseille massacre. Now, hearing the Romanian Foreign Minister's debate, they could only remain silent and feign composure, which was somewhat awkward.

The League of Nations was originally a machine for the great powers to divide the spoils. It might have some means of resolving disputes between small and weak countries, and it might have the authority to make judgments. However, if it encountered a powerful country causing trouble, it could be said that there was absolutely no solution. For example, during the [September 18th Incident] in our country, our representative eloquently spoke at several League of Nations meetings, directly stating justice and fairness. However, the League of Nations council members were ultimately unable to take action and could only look at the ceiling, pick their teeth, and frequently examine their fingernails. What other solutions were there? Therefore, the League of Nations' [paper tiger] had long been pierced by the Japanese. What else could it do? As the saying goes, [One cannot be an elder if one is not foolish and deaf.] This is the best attitude for the League of Nations Council members to adopt. Although this attitude is similar to mine when I take a bath, the reproach in their consciences must cause some hidden pain, some [embarrassment]. If a [photograph] of the council members were taken at this time, it would certainly be interesting.

Saigon Shore

— Li Dan

The ship drifted past the Seven Islands Sea, and the dark black seawater gradually turned light green. Green mountains also appeared vaguely in the distance. The travelers on board, who were heading to Nanyang to make a living, their vague hopes were gradually turning into more concrete joy. A large group of newcomers who had never tasted the life of a ["foreign guest"] were even more swayed by dreams of yellow gold. They were filled with fresh hope of being a ["foreign guest"]! To go to a foreign land to be a ["foreign guest"] and make money! Although the foreign land was somewhat hazy and elusive, it was, after all, the birthplace of many wealthy people in their hometowns. Therefore, many of them sold their children into debt to raise the fare, their hearts filled with bitterness, yet they came with surprise.

The ship entered the port, and the travelers' moods were even more lively. The seventy-nine bends along the harbor were so beautiful and winding, like a long snake crawling in a winding manner. Countless harbors passed one after another. Both sides were lush with green grass. There were no tall trees in the high sky, only a vast expanse of dense green. Interspersed in the middle were some thatched houses, without the tall buildings like in their homeland. These were the poor dwellings of the Vietnamese natives. The scenery was different from that of their homeland.

After passing the seventy-nine bends, the towering buildings of the customs and merchants on the Saigon shore stood before them. They had arrived in the foreign land! The travelers had long packed their luggage, waiting to leave the tiresome ship and climb to their destination to experience new tastes. However, their fervent hopes gradually turned weary. The ship had docked for a long time, but there was still no movement. Apart from some overseas Chinese who came to pick up guests, the French and Vietnamese people in front of the customs walked around as if nothing had happened. As if they had nothing to do with the anxious guests on the ship.

First, the Japanese freely went ashore, strutting into Saigon city without going through the ["New Guest Office"]. Next, the wealthy and shop owners with street license taxes had bribed people in advance to have their relatives and friends pick them up with joy.

Page 18

What remained was the largest number of impoverished people. They could not bribe people in advance, so they could only wait anxiously. However, time passed, and there was still no response, only their own unease and commotion increased dramatically. Inevitably, impatient and worried voices arose:

"What's going on?"

"Why can't we go ashore yet?"

However, the area in front of the customs remained quiet. No French or Annamese people approached the ship. They gazed eagerly, but their gazes fell on the empty ground, wandering aimlessly. Children cried on the ship, and women murmured.

It was noon, with the sun blazing, when the French entered the New Guest Office to work. The travelers on the ship had been waiting for half a day. Standing in the intense sunlight, they were dazed and exhausted, their legs sore and their arms weak, but they still had to wait patiently. These guests were guarded by the Annamese people who had lost their country, waiting for the French to complete the entry procedures.

The sunlight near the equator was hotter than in their homeland. This was the first new taste of the foreign land they experienced. Waiting to go to the New Guest Office would bring even more trouble. By the time the ship reached the Saigon shore, they had already lost their admiration for being a "foreign guest" and could not help but think of their families in their hometown. They sighed that a foreign land was not as good as their homeland! But they also saw the Japanese and wealthy Chinese people, who were in a different situation altogether.

Night Watchmen, Street Singers, Fortune Tellers

— Feng

| Impressions of Beiping, Part Four

The ancient city, like an old man, went to rest early, exhausted from its accumulated fatigue. The night in the ancient city was lonely, unlike the bustling all-night activity in other cities; this loneliness came very early.

In the loneliness, there were three kinds of people struggling: night watchmen, street singers, and fortune tellers. The three kinds of people used three different sounds to express their activities: a clapper, a sanxian lute, and a xiao flute. They all had a mournful tone.

At eight o'clock, the sudden sound of the clapper could be heard in the lonely alley—this was the first watch. When you heard the clapper rhythmically sounding five times, five times, that was the fifth watch, around four or five in the morning, when it was almost dawn. Regardless of wind, snow, or night, the watchmen always followed the dark alleys, turning corner after corner, constantly watching every household's gate. If it was open, they would wake up the owner of the gate: "Hey, be careful, close it." Then they would continue with their rhythmic clapper sound. The sound was a warning, but small businesses working at night would gradually submit when they heard the sound getting closer. The watchmen held a bamboo pole with a hook. This bamboo pole aroused many imaginations in me: a timid thief crouching on the black wall, a ladder leaning against someone's wall, or a black coat hanging on a telephone pole against the wall... let the dim light in their hands illuminate them...

The sound was also a comfort, with a spirited courage in the sound of the clapper, like the guardian of the sleeping people. However, in the ears of those who could not sleep, the sound was reckless. Tossing and turning, just when they were planning not to calculate the time, the sound would knock into your heart, telling you what time it was.

The sound of the clapper still had a bit of courageous breath, but the sanxian lute and the xiao flute only had begging tones. In the mournfulness, there seemed to be some sobbing.

Those playing the sanxian lute often brought young girls, and sometimes, this person would be the girl's family member. They always played the same tune, occasionally hitting a large drum. The so-called large drum was actually not very large. It was placed in front of the girl when she was about to sing, supported on a triangular frame to keep the girl's rhythm. Their activity area was mostly near apartments and hostels. Tired guests or wanderers sometimes had the need to talk to a woman. ["Waiter, call in the drum player."] In the fifteen-candlepower electric-lit room of the apartment, they bargained about the price, ordered songs, and did that uninteresting and necessary work. After it was over,

Page 19

[Give a few extra coins for drinks, sir." the lute player pleaded, then walked out of the apartment door and played the same tune on another] street, still sobbing.

The sound of the xiao flute contained more resentment in the sobbing, as if resenting the ups and downs of fate? However, they were fortune tellers. Why were fortune tellers mostly blind? I didn't understand. They held a bamboo cane, touching the uneven ground. They should know the height of the ground, and they never doubted their foothold, walking forward step by step, like the resentment that fate had destined. They were calculating other people's fates, knowing which old man was born in which year, and which girl would marry in which year; but they seemed not to calculate their own fates, they only resented.

How to Choose Magazines and How to Read Magazines?

— Zhang Yuqing

Because this year is magazine year, the number of magazines will reach more than six hundred. From the perspective of the entire culture, this is something worth celebrating - indeed, it breaks the strange phenomenon of the distorted culture of China in previous years. However, for those of us suffering from knowledge hunger, how should we choose magazines and how should we read magazines?

Indeed, there are too many modern books, and at the same time, the expensive prices are really beyond the reach of those below the middle class - and modern life is very busy. It is really not easy for those who are busy with life to take some time to seek knowledge! The first principle is to take the most economical method that my own financial ability can afford; the second is to take the most practical knowledge, with the knowledge I need as the goal, then only magazines are suitable.

Looking at the sales of magazines and the stagnation of books in recent years, most of the reason is, of course, due to the weak purchasing power of the majority of people. Although not every single book is bad, and not every single magazine is good, in short, Chinese society has first become distorted, and then this strange phenomenon of distorted culture has occurred.

How to choose magazines and how to read magazines? Perhaps many readers already understand, or perhaps some people really need such an answer? However, I am very frank to say: I am not a famous scholar, and the motivation for me to write this article now is nothing more than to talk about some of my own feelings about reading magazines.

First of all, before we open a magazine and are about to read it, we should first recognize whether this magazine is the magazine I need. The reason is that the content of a magazine is more complicated than that of a book, and at the same time it also has specialized properties, so what should it be like? Naturally, first of all we should know the common sense of magazine classification, but however, this distinction is very difficult. I have seen someone say this: [There are so many magazines that it is really difficult for people to distinguish between good and bad at once! And it is always inevitable that the people who run magazines have a background. Of course, they have received money from others, so they cannot help but say a few words for the people who paid the money? However, many writers use pen names, and it is really easy to be deceived when it is first published, so you often have to see their details after the expiration date, and the content is finally explained by itself.] Therefore, when we have a magazine in hand, we should first distinguish the content of this magazine. Of course, magazines and writers who stand on a purely objective position are not completely non-existent.

As for how to read magazines? However, there are only four ways to read magazines: (1) Read all: that is, to read a magazine completely, regardless of whether you need it or not, read it all once to understand the entire content of the magazine. (2) Selective reading: Read what you love or what you really need. (3) Speed reading: be more casual than reading everything, more like interesting essays and novels, so as to understand the general content of the whole article. (4) Read carefully: every article should be read carefully, like the attitude of a critic, using a calm mind and discerning eyes to measure the content of the magazine, but do not add your own subjective opinions, and stand in a purely objective position.

Sunbathing

— Yi An

Solitude

— Rui

The cold wind whipped across the quiet road surface, and withered yellow leaves tumbled on the ground. He paced slowly, feeling lonely and depressed in his heart. He was thinking, thinking about the past, the present, and what about the future? He could only look at the dark sky and the quiet road, feeling lost. ["Will it always be like this?"] He often asked himself this question, but who could give him an answer? Only the wind, tightly whipping the road surface, echoed in his ears, as if saying: ["Your future is just like you running on this road now."]

The black hand of night tightly touched the head of the city, and darkness occupied the world before his eyes. He stared blankly, watching the lights of the bustling streets in the distance. He hated it, hated it. Everything made him feel sad, understanding that this hatred, this hate, were all superfluous, all thoughts that a lonely person should not have. He understood that a few years ago, when he was living a happy life, he saw those, those things that were now placed in his eyes were lovely, how madly he pursued them. However, people's psychology is selfish and insufficient. When he had such a joyful environment, he never thought of those people who were in the same situation as he is now. But now, it had changed, the environment had changed, his feelings had also changed, and he only felt his own sadness and loneliness. A person, like him, was just so selfish.

[Fallen, right! I am just so lonely, the sadness of the end of the petty bourgeoisie!]

He closed his tired eyes, shook the old autumn clothes on his body, lay down on the cold bed, and sank into the dream sea of ​​memories.

He thought, he dreamed, he remembered a winter night in Chengdao City.

Winter in the island city was lovely, warm, and beautiful. It was a clear afternoon, he was holding Apple's hand, walking slowly on the beach, bathing in the sunlight, listening to the faint whistling of the tide. The shallow sand on the beach was a stretch of white, and he and she were walking slowly along the curve of the bay.

[Let's walk again! This is the last time you see the scenery of this island city. Go and hope, I intend to leave here one day, to spend a winter, that severe winter, and be with you at the same time.]

He seemed to be drunk, he didn't feel anything, he should how to answer her, how to say some comforting words to her, he just looked at that under his feet, he felt depressed and lonely, he felt such a mood for the first time.

The sun was jumping on the vast deep blue water, as if telling people; [It's almost evening, happy people! Leave here! The night of the city is waiting for you to enjoy, there are all your world, don't be drunk! Happy people.]

The cold wind pierced into her body, he understood, he woke up, he knew that it was the past. He opened his eyes and looked at the dark house. Everything was blurred and silent before his eyes. He stretched his waist and looked out the window. What was placed before his hatred was the prosperous night of the city, the bright night, the night of the happy, and the intoxicating night.

Lonely, lonely, he only felt the loneliness of life even more, and he murmured again!

[No way, right! I am just so lonely, the sadness of the end of the petty bourgeoisie!]

National Studies

Ms. Wang Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Elegy Part One Yuan Zhen

Lord Xie doted on his youngest daughter especially, but after marrying her to the poor, everything went wrong.

Caring for me without clothes, she searched the coffers; to press him to buy wine, she pulled out her golden hairpin.

Wild vegetables filled the meal, sweetly eating long vegetables; fallen leaves added to the fire, looking up at the ancient locust tree.

Today, my salary exceeds ten thousand, and I hold memorial services and offer斋 for you.

Part Two

In the past, jokes were made about matters after death, but now they have all come before me.

The clothes have already been given away and almost all are seen; the needlework still remains and I cannot bear to open it.

I still think of the old feelings and pity the servants; I have also sent money in dreams.

I truly know that everyone has this regret; poverty and lowly wife, a hundred things are sad.

Part Three

Sitting idly, I grieve for you and also for myself; how long is a hundred years? Deng You had no son and sought to know his fate; Pan Yue mourned his dead wife and still wasted words.

What hope is there in the dark abyss of the same grave? It is even harder to expect a缘会 in the next life.

I will only keep my eyes open all night long to repay the unfulfilled眉 of my life.

Shanghai Shen Bao Local Supplement Automotive Weekly

American Cars Re-enter the European Market

— Shirley

| Exports have doubled in the past six months |

In the past 22 years, Europe has suffered from economic depression. Various industries have been severely hit. The decline in social economy and the unemployment of workers are innumerable. In order to remedy any possible situation, the government has adopted a strict attitude towards the intrusion of foreign goods. Either high tariff barriers are built, or taxes are increased. Countries like France, Italy, and Germany have used this method to resist the entry of foreign cars. On the one hand, it can limit the outflow of money, and on the other hand, it can relieve unemployed workers in the country. Considering the economic relations of various countries, it is of course not too strong. This situation seemed to change slightly until this spring. Because the economic situation in Europe has slightly improved, and various industries have also improved accordingly. Afterwards, the situation improved day by day. Until recently, the European car market has undergone a major change. Among them, the position of American cars has increased day by day. Originally, the sales were stagnant, but now they feel very active. Originally, people could not afford to buy them, but now they are eager to try. Moreover, many large American cars are selling well in Europe. It is expected that the situation will continue to improve in the future.

Among the European countries that manufacture cars, the United Kingdom, France, and Italy are the most developed. Because the United Kingdom's machinery industry is developed and its territorial exports are more abundant, its car industry is even better than that of France and Italy. In recent years, the United Kingdom has seized the opportunity of various countries to reduce the purchase of American cars and has been working hard to gain a more dominant car market in Europe. Originally, this opportunity was very good, and it has already achieved some success. Unfortunately, the current situation has changed, and the original hope has inevitably become a bubble. Because in fact, American cars in Europe have not only recovered the market they have lost recently, but also have the possibility of increasing it. At the same time, the British car market in Europe has suffered a major blow. This point cannot but worry British car manufacturers. In addition, in the past three or four months, the British domestic car market has been invaded by American cars. American cars are also selling well in other territories. Originally, this part of trade could be regarded as the private property of the British, but now it has been seized by the Americans. How can British car merchants not be sweating?

According to the statistics of British car manufacturers, in the first six months of 1934, the number of cars exported from the United States to Europe, excluding Great Britain, totaled 27,000. As for the cars manufactured in the United Kingdom and exported to European countries, there were only 5,643. The total number of British car exports includes 1,365 cars exported to the Irish Free State. This market is extremely beneficial to the British car market. As for American cars, they are almost completely unable to enter Ireland. The reason for this is easy to understand. Because the government of the Irish Free State now prohibits the import of all foreign cars. It can be seen that American cars not only have no way to enter Ireland at present, but it is also difficult to predict the future situation for a while. Therefore, in the first six months of this year, although the United States had 30,000 complete cars imported into European countries, only 198 went to Ireland. Compared with the total number, it is less than one percent.

In the first half of 1934, from January to June, Belgium was the country where American cars sold the best in the European market. Although Belgium levies a very high import tax on foreign cars, it purchased 9,751 cars from the United States in these six months. The Swedish car market has been noticed by British car manufacturers in recent years. In half a year, it purchased 5,463 American cars. It bought only 433 mobility products from Great Britain. The comparison between the two is very different. Speaking of the United Kingdom itself, it is the third-best customer for buying American cars in Europe. In the first six months of this year, the United Kingdom imported a total of 3,759 American cars. In addition, American cars imported 3,362 cars into Denmark and 2,638 into the Netherlands. Only 328 British cars were imported. 1,580 American cars were imported into Switzerland, but only 141 British cars were imported.

If we take the world as a whole, the number of American cars exported to various countries around the world in the first six months of 1934 has increased by more than double compared with the same period in 1933. As of the end of June 1934, the United States had more than doubled. As of the end of June 1934, the number of privately-owned cars sold by the United States overseas reached 78,636. In the same period in 1933, it was 33,386. Adding the 30,000 cars purchased by European countries, 28,316 of them were purchased by various parts of the United Kingdom.

The automotive industry in Great Britain itself is also quite developed at present. However, in some periods in the past, the number of American cars imported into the United Kingdom was very small. There are two reasons for this. One is the implementation of the horsepower tax, which greatly reduced the sales of large cars. The second is the tariff barrier. Foreign cars are inevitably hit. In addition, factors such as the poor social economy and the increase in the number of unemployed are closely related. Therefore, the sales of American cars in the United Kingdom can be said to be dripping. As for the specifics, the situation has changed. The number of American cars imported into the United States has increased fivefold this year compared with last year. According to official statistics, from January 1 to September 30 this year, a total of 5,234 American cars were sold in the United Kingdom. In the same period of nine months last year, it was 1,430 cars. The United Kingdom also imported 2,240 cars from its territories. The original manufacturers of these cars were the United States. However, in order to reduce the tax from 33 and one-third percent to 25 percent, they were assembled in Canada and transshipped to the United Kingdom. In the past, the United Kingdom collected a tax of 33 and one-third percent on the import of foreign-made cars. And those from Canada can enjoy special benefits. Therefore, these cars seem to be exported from Canada on the surface, but in reality, they are transshipped goods from the United States. Canada purchased 171 French automobiles and 113 automobiles from other countries in the world.

1935 Model Austin New Car

— Fu

｜Already Arrived in Shanghai｜

I have considered that the Austin Motor Company has its own definite and unwavering policy for the construction of new cars, and is not blindly following and echoing others, merely changing designs for the sake of it. Because of this, the company has exhausted its thoughts and carefully studied the matter, and after manufacturing a truly reliable vehicle, it does not act rashly or change it easily, hoping to show off its novelty and originality. Even if there are slight changes in each year, they are all mainly to meet public needs. The reason why Austin's value and reliability have always enjoyed a great reputation in the world is that this policy is one of its major reasons. Now, the 1935 model Austin new car has arrived in Shanghai. Here is a brief description of its general situation, as follows, to be offered to readers.

The Austin factory believes that what is needed this year is a more spacious body, rather than major changes in the mechanical aspects. Therefore, there are currently no so-called streamlined sedans or independent suspensions. Regarding streamlined sedans, Sir Austin once expressed his opinion that the sloping screens installed on this type of body are suitable for obstructing the driver's vision. However, the Austin new car does not have such shortcomings. The slight changes made to the new car are that the body lines are longer, and the posture is more graceful and natural. As for the newly designed water tank shell and the long engine hood, they make the entire form extremely beautiful and spectacular. The various facilities are more uniform and unified than before, and they are all inlaid in the body, so the overall appearance is more clean and elegant, without any cumbersomeness. As for the chassis, the main improvement in the mechanical engineering of the 1935 model Austin new car is that the second gear shift, the third gear, and the final gear all use synchronized shifting. According to Sir Austin's speech on this reform, the factory believes it is insignificant and unnecessary. It is only because the public likes this device that it is specially installed on the new car to meet the needs of the public. As for the Hayes gearbox, it has already won the admiration of the general public at the last exhibition and is recognized as a unique feature of Austin. However, due to various difficulties in production, it has not been fully utilized. Now, production has greatly increased, and both the 16 and 18 horsepower models can be equipped with it. Although the Austin new car has the above-mentioned improvements, the selling price is roughly the same as before, with little change. Among them, the 7-horsepower model is the most commendable. In terms of price, it has a considerable reduction, while in terms of quality, its various improvements and great progress are unmatched by other similar vehicles. Its chassis is particularly low, and the floor height is more than five inches lower than before. The rear of the body is spacious, twice as large as before. Both front seats can be folded forward for easy entry and exit, and it is extremely convenient to adjust their position separately to enjoy the ultimate comfort. Both doors are extremely wide, and the window frames are unusually narrow. The driver sits in the seat, and everything he sees is unobstructed. The body is equipped with wheel covers and luggage clips, all of which are hidden inside and do not hinder the appearance at all.

In addition to these various changes, there are embedded direction indicators, a convenient steering wheel manager, larger tires, a battery hidden under the engine hood, and excellent drive shafts. The ease of management and the convenience of operation are enough to surprise the driver. As for those who are economically minded and want to enjoy the pleasure of riding in a car at the lowest cost, there is the Austin Opal two-seater, which retails for only 100 pounds in its country, equipped with an old-fashioned water tank, with the same appearance as the product from last year.

The above-mentioned progress and changes are not only for the small Austin but also for the larger cars. The 1-horsepower four-cylinder model has exceeded 50,000 units in output. The new equipment includes a balanced voltmeter, double windshield wipers, new headlights, and a heat-preserving and cold-preserving device. The sedan body is wider and more spacious than before. The lightweight 12-horsepower model can use either a 12.9-horsepower four-cylinder engine or a 13.9 or 15.9-horsepower six-cylinder engine. If a larger chassis is needed, there are 16-horsepower and 18-horsepower models. The台約克轿车 (Tái Yuēkè Jiàochē, could not translate) is the newest model added. All of these models can be equipped with temporary seats, so they can accommodate up to seven passengers without feeling cramped. Moreover, the rear seats are extremely easy to adjust, making them particularly easy to control. Furthermore, these cars can be equipped with Hayes gearboxes if needed. As for the 12-horsepower four-cylinder model, it has also been equipped with synchronized two-gear shifts, but all the management devices remain the same and have not been changed. Finally, it must be mentioned that the 20-horsepower model is a large car of magnificent splendor. In addition to all the latest progress of the other Austin new cars, it also has a strong and outstanding low-slung X-shaped frame and a new steering gear.

Regarding overseas sales, the Austin new car also has many features. For example, all models, except for the 12-horsepower four-cylinder and 20-horsepower models, can be equipped with left-hand steering wheels and management devices, special ground clearance, special suspension and tires, and three-layer thick glass. These are all the major features.

As for the Austin truck group, it includes a 7-horsepower model with a load capacity of five CWt·, a 10-horsepower four-cylinder model with six to eight Cwt·, a lightweight 12-horsepower six-cylinder, and a lightweight 12-horsepower four-cylinder model with various chassis. All of these vehicles only use synchronized final gear and three-gear shifts. In addition to this, there are ambulance chassis and 12-horsepower four-cylinder bus chassis equipped with inverted rear springs to lower the body frame.

Page 22

As for Austin sports cars, there are a total of five types: the Nimble 7-horsepower, the Express 7-horsepower, the 10-horsepower four-cylinder律普萊式 (Lǜ Pǔlái Shì, could not translate), the 紐勃里運動篷車 (Niǔ Bólǐ Yùndòng Péngchē, could not translate), and the 坎姆登運動轎車 (Kǎnmǔdēng Yùndòng Jiàochē, could not translate) equipped with a 12-horsepower six-cylinder.

The Standard New Car is the Soul of British Cars

(1) The Beauty of Performance

The 1935 Standard new car is unanimously recognized by the general British public as the soul of British cars. The so-called 1935 Standard car has now arrived in Shanghai and is on display in the model room of the China Motor Company on Jing'an Temple Road. The 1935 Standard 9-horsepower four-door exquisite sedan, due to its fuel economy and smooth driving, will be considered satisfactory by any car owner. In fact, this new car is a representative product of the British automobile industry's efforts. The clear lines and proper control, after the new car is constructed, have achieved such results. The engine is a four-cylinder, with a volume of 1.052 cubic centimeters. When it rotates 1,000 times per minute, the plug force can reach 18 horsepower, and when it rotates 3,000 times per minute, it can reach 23 horsepower. A single-piece dry clutch and a four-speed two-wheel box make the engine completely use a buoyancy device, that is, there are also two points in the front, all supported by rubber pads.

(2) The Completeness of Accessories

The carburetor adopts a mixed gas temperature control, and the result can save cylinder wear during long-distance travel. The ignition point and distribution can be automatic. Water gates, spark plugs, oil pool dipsticks, inverted coils, external oil pools, etc. are all perfectly placed on the side of the valve. The fan and generator are driven by the same belt. After the generator starts, the belt will automatically tighten. The gasoline input to the carburetor has a pump mechanism, which is placed on the outside like the generator. The parts box and battery are placed on the instrument panel, and there is a cam rotation. Gears two, three, and the highest gear are synchronized. The open drive shaft has a metal joint, and the關浮式 (Guān Fú Shì, could not translate) rear axle is equipped with灣拿齒輪 (Wān Ná Chǐlún, could not translate) drive. The frame uses a crossbar, which is very strong, and the plug itself can generate power. During operation, the hand lever and foot pedal are placed in front of the front seat, which is very convenient and within easy reach. The device uses semi-elliptical springs with hydraulic shock absorbers. The frame and springs are all under the rear axle.

(3) The Swiftness of Driving

This new car performs exceptionally well. Even if you travel across the entire territory of the United Kingdom, you can obtain a rate above the standard. Second gear: 28 miles per hour; third gear: 40 miles; highest gear: 55 miles. The rear wheel axle ratio is five, five-seven to one. Without special acceleration, you can also reach a considerable rate. The engine's action is very smooth. The test drive has found that all the control is very convenient. The weight of the entire car is 17 CWT·. The factory estimates that one gallon of gasoline can travel approximately 38 miles. The wheelbase is seven feet six and a half inches, and the track is three feet ten inches.

(4) The Ten-Horsepower New Car

Among the Standard new cars, in addition to the exquisite 9-horsepower car, the next is the 10-horsepower new car. The engine has a three-bearing crankshaft, water pump circulation. When the engine rotates 3,600 times per minute, the plug force can reach 32 horsepower. Among the various modern devices and accessories, there are automatic engine restart reserve瓦脱 (Wǎtuō, could not translate) control, which allows the battery to supply power as needed, so power waste can be avoided. The springs have silent coupling shaft sleeves, window switches, pure steel safety body, and the windshield can be centrally controlled. Both front and rear seats have 睹藏馬逹 (Dǔcáng Mǎdá, could not translate) for opening and closing the door and window curtains. The engine is also a four-cylinder, with a volume of 1.343 cubic centimeters. All gear ratios are 5.43, 7.88, 13.18, 21.42 to 1. The diameter of the plug drum is eight時｜｜與九四相同｜ (Shí ｜｜ Yǔ Jiǔ Sì Xiāngtóng ｜, could not translate) weighs 19 CWT, the wheelbase is seven feet ten時 (Shí, could not translate), and the track is three feet ten inches.

A Record of [The Advance of the Wheels]

— Cheng Zhizheng

The利喴 (Lì Wēi, could not translate) Motor Company screened the business propaganda film [The Advance of the Wheels] produced by the British Austin Motor Manufacturing Factory at the Carlton Theater on the 9th. It was advertised in the newspapers in advance, welcoming people from all walks of life to visit. That day happened to be a weekly holiday. At 10 o'clock in the morning, the visitors were already crowded, and both the upstairs and downstairs were full. There were even people who came with the elderly and children. Its grand occasion was unprecedented. I went to the theater and was found a seat with the help of the receptionists. There were still hundreds of people who were standing because there were no seats, and those who had nowhere to stand had to leave. Its appeal is also great.

The screening started at half past ten. The first scene was a family background. The father was sitting by the stove, and the son was studying at his desk. He asked his father about the traffic situation in the past. From his father's narration, the contrast between today's and yesterday's traffic was shown. First, there was a horse-drawn carriage, and the passengers in the carriage were very crowded. After a while of galloping, they suffered a lot of bumps. Then, the first invented car was shown, and then the modern car was shown, some of which were ridden by individuals, and some were double-decker for public riding. The richness and comfort of them cannot be compared with the past. Then, the earliest train was shown. The passenger car where the passengers were sitting had no awnings and no windows, just like a side car for transporting stone ballast. There were many passengers inside, all squatting in the car. When getting off the car, they used short wooden ladders to help each other to get off. Compared with today's passengers who can read books and newspapers and eat Western food in the car, it is like heaven and earth.

After comparing the old and new means of transportation, the internal working conditions of the Austin factory were shown. Whether it was the body, wheels, engine, etc., even as small as a steel rod or a crank, the manufacturing process was shown in detail. After the car was completed, it was painted, packed, and exported, all of which were presented in front of us. Even if we personally visited the factory, its authenticity would be no more than this. The factory covers an area of 93 acres, has 16,000 workers, and 600 supervisors, which is the largest in Europe. What is particularly noteworthy is that the painting department is all female workers. When working, they use the car body as a mirror and frequently take care of their hair, which is enough to show the brightness of the car body.

After the various departments in the factory were shown, the miracle of climbing mountains produced by the factory was shown. The mountain was the high peak of Norway, covered with snow, and it was extremely difficult to climb. However, the car finally reached its summit, and the excellence of its mechanical power can be generally seen.

Then, there was a sweet family, a couple with two children taking a suburban tour in an Austin car, enjoying the fun of nature in a forest. There were also those who drove with their companions to swim by the sea, all feeling content. In short, all of this reveals the need for cars for the people and the necessity of owning them.

Finally, there was a famous British landscape film, with clear mountains and rivers, which made people feel relaxed and yearning, almost as if they were in the scene. It is found that advertising-style propaganda films are the most difficult to arouse the interest of the audience, because their materials are narrow and have a dull taste. This film alone uses a novel story narrative, supplemented by beautiful landscape photography, and puts business propaganda unconsciously. This is truly a mirror for various automobile manufacturers. Therefore, I recorded what I remembered.
